<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-competence">Module competence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-competence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This module is designed to enable the learner to acquire knowledge, skills and attitude in midwifery so as to be able to promote healthy pregnancy, provide quality care during pregnancy, labour and puerperium for a woman as well as to the newborn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-units">Module units<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>S.N</th><th>UNITS</th><th>HOURS THEORY</th><th>PRACTICUM</th><th>LECTURER</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1.</td><td>Normal Pregnancy</td><td>04</td><td>00</td><td>MR. RUGENDO.M.M</td></tr><tr><td>2.</td><td>Normal Labour</td><td>14</td><td>00</td><td>MR. RUGENDO.M.M</td></tr><tr><td>3.</td><td>Normal Puerperium</td><td>06</td><td>00</td><td>M/S J. WACHIRA</td></tr><tr><td>4.</td><td>Normal Baby</td><td>06</td><td>00</td><td>M/S J. WACHIRA</td></tr><tr><td>Module Learning Outcomes</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>At the end of this module, the learner should be able to: -</p>
<ol>
<li>Identify mothers with normal pregnancy</li>
<li>Provide appropriate antenatal care</li>
<li>Conduct and manage safe delivery</li>
<li>Provide care to mothers during puerperium period</li>
<li>Provide essential newborn care.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-content">Module Content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Normal Pregnancy: Definition, Terminologies, pillars and concepts in MNH (Preconception care), essential obstetric and newborn care, physiological changes during pregnancy, physical, emotional/psychological changes during pregnancy, history taking, physical examination (General examination, abdominal examination, breast examination, vaginal examination), Focused Antenatal Care (FANC), estimation of gestational age, diagnosis of pregnancy, Individualized Birth Plan, health messages shared during pregnancy, eMTCT, danger signs during pregnancy, minor disorders during pregnancy.</li>
<li>Normal Labour: Definition (labour, normal labour), admitting a mother into labour ward (history taking, general physical examination, breast examination, abdominal examination, vaginal examination, pelvic examination weight, vital signs, laboratory investigations), documentation, characteristics of normal labour, diagnosis of labour, true &amp; false labour, premonitory signs of labour, physiology of the onset of labour, mechanisms of labour, stages of labour, physiological changes in all stage of</li>
</ol>
<p>1 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>labour, 4Ps, management of all stages of labour, use of partograph, Active Management of Third Stage of Labour (AMTSL), pain management.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Normal Puerperium: Definition, physiological and Emotional changes during puerperium, Targeted postnatal care, physiology of lactation, psychosocial care, immediate and subsequent management of the mother, health messages, postnatal danger signs. eMTCT, Infant feeding methods (exclusive breastfeeding, cup and spoon), minor complications of puerperium.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Normal Baby: APGAR Scoring, physiological adaptation of a newborn, characteristics of a normal newborn, immediate and subsequent management of the newborn (warm chain, administration of Tetracycline Eye Ointment and Vitamin K, initiation of breastfeeding, cord care, care of the eyes, immunization), First examination of the newborn, daily(routine) examination of the newborn danger signs.</p>
</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This part of lecture notes provides learners with necessary knowledge on how to manage a woman with normal pregnancy, normal labour, normal puerperium and how to manage a normal neonate. It is expected that after acquiring these concepts in normal midwifery you will be able to provide quality care to pregnant women, women in labour and postnatal mothers with their babies.</p>
<p>Kindly consult the course coordinators in case you have clarification on this module.</p>
<p>3 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition-of-terminologies">Definition of terminologies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terminologies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pregnancy-This is a term used to refer to the maternal condition of having a developing fetus in the uterus.</p>
<p>Normal pregnancy - refer to the maternal condition of having a single developing fetus in the uterus with no associated complications both to the mother and the fetus.</p>
<p>Obstetrics- This a branch of medicine that deals with the care of women's reproductive health, pregnancy, labour and postnatal period.</p>
<p>Embryo- It is a term used to refer to developing conceptus from fertilization to 8th week of pregnancy.</p>
<p>Foetus-it is the term used to refer to developing conceptus from 8th week of gestation until delivery.</p>
<p>Gestational age- Refers to the duration of pregnancy mostly calculated from the first day of the last (normal) menstrual period(LMP). Gestational age is expressed in terms of completed weeks.</p>
<p>Gravid-Means the state of being pregnant.</p>
<p>Gravidity(Gravida)-Means the total number of pregnancies both normal or abnormal. It can also be defined as the number of times the mother has been pregnant regardless of whether the pregnancies were carried to term or not. The current pregnancy is always included in the gravidity.</p>
<p>Nulligravida- A woman who has never been pregnant.</p>
<p>Multigravida-This is a term that refers to a woman who has been pregnant more than one time.</p>
<p>Parity-It is the state of having given birth to an infant after the age of viability (28 weeks in Kenya) or an infant weighing 500gms or more whether alive or dead.</p>
<p>Gestation-It refers to the state of carrying an embryo/foetus in the uterus.</p>
<p>Trimester- This refers to the way of dividing pregnancy into three distinct periods; namely:</p>
<p>a) First trimester-period between first and 12th week of gestation.
b) Second trimester- Period between 13th week to 28th week of gestation.
c) Third trimester- Period from 29th week of gestation until delivery.</p>
<p>Live birth- It refers to complete expulsion or extraction of product of conception that shows evidence of life (eg heart rate, pulsation of umbilical cord, observable movements of involuntary muscles) regardless of the duration of pregnancy.</p>
<p>Infant- This is a term that refers to a live-born individual from birth until completion of one year of life.</p>
<p>Preterm infant- Any fetus born between 28th-37th weeks of gestation.</p>
<p>Miscarriage (Abortion)-Refers to termination of pregnancy before viability (28 weeks of gestation). There are various causes of miscarriage (This will be covered in details in gynecological nursing) which may include: -</p>
<p>a) Chromosomal abnormalities
b) Malformed uterus
c) Foetal congenital abnormalities.
d) Cervical weakness
e) Hormonal disorders
f) Severe infections</p>
<p>Types of miscarriage(Abortion):</p>
<p>6 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>a) Threatened
b) Inevitable
c) Complete
d) Missed
e) Septic
f) Recurrent/habitual</p>
<p>Presentation-This refers which anatomical part of the uterus is closest to the pelvic inlet of the birth canal during pregnancy or just before birth.</p>
<p>Lie- This is the relationship of the longitudinal axis of the fetus to the longitudinal axis of the mother (Lie can be longitudinal, oblique, transverse).</p>
<p>Station-This refers to the relationship of the fetal presenting part to ischial spines.</p>
<p>Attitude-Refers to the relationship of foetal parts to its trunk (The normal attitude is flexed one).</p>
<p>Moulding -Refers to the process through which fetal skull bones come closer to each other due to pelvic forces when the fetal head is moving through the pelvis during delivery. Moulding enables reduction of fetal skull diameter and encourages progress of delivery through maternal pelvis. However, in some circumstances moulding can be excessive. Moulding has therefore been graded as follows:</p>
<p>0 If bones are separated and the sutures can be felt easily</p>
<ul>
<li>If sutures are apposed but no overlap i.e. the bones are just touching each other
++ If there is overlapping of the sutures but it is reducible
+++ If the sutures overlap but not reducible</li>
</ul>
<p>Effacement- It is the process through which cervix shortens as it becomes included in the lower uterine segment.</p>
<p>Engagement- Engagement is said to have taken place when the widest part of the presenting part of the fetus has successfully passed through the pelvic inlet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-of-pregnancy">Diagnosis of pregnancy.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The average duration of pregnancy 280 days or 40 weeks. To correctly calculate you need to get first day of the last Normal Menstrual Period.</p>
<p>Diagnosis of pregnancy can be made through the following approaches: -</p>
<p>a) History taking
b) Physical examination
c) Laboratory investigations (e.g Pregnancy test)
d) Radiological tests (X-Ray, U/S)
e) Signs and symptoms.</p>
<p>This part of the lecture will discuss Signs and Symptoms of pregnancy in details. Each student it read more on other approaches in diagnosing pregnancy.</p>
<p>7 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Signs and symptoms of pregnancy.</p>
<p>Signs and symptoms of pregnancy are categorized into three groups, namely;</p>
<p>a) Possible signs (Presumptive signs)
b) Probable signs
c) Positive signs (Confirmatory signs)</p>
<p>a) Possible signs (Presumptive signs)</p>
<p>These are signs reported by the woman. They are signs that accompanies pregnancy but there are other causes to these signs other than pregnancy. These signs include: -</p>
<p>Amenorrhea (4 weeks +) but may have other causes e.g. stress. Breastfeeding, menopause, anemia, contraceptive use, emotional stress.</p>
<p>Morning sickness (4 â€“ 14 weeks) especially nausea and vomiting from 6 weeks due to gastric upset related to HcG production. Differential diagnosis is indigestion, emotional stress or appendicitis.</p>
<p>Frequency in micturition/Bladder irritability (6 â€“ 12 weeks) due to increased vascularity and pressure on the bladder. Other than pregnancy this can be caused by Diabetes Mellitus, Urinary tract infections or Urinary system tumors.</p>
<p>Breast changes (3-4 weeks +) e.g. increased vascularity, primary areola become more pigmented and the Montgomery tubercles are more marked. However this can be caused by hormonal changes, contraceptive use among others.</p>
<p>Skin changes at external genitalia and anal area become darker due to increased vascularity. At 12 weeks, abdomen may have striae and linea nigra. Skin changes in pregnancy is mainly due to increased production or sensitivity to adrenocortical hormone during pregnancy. Skin changes may not be definitive sign of pregnancy since it can occur due to Cushing's syndrome or in sudden weight loss. Other skin changes seen in pregnancy include: -Chloasma, Linea nigra, Striae gravidarum, stretch marks and spider telangiectasia.</p>
<p>Quickening (16-20 weeks) â€“ is a feeling of life within the uterus and occurs at about 16 weeks' gestation. This can also be caused by intestinal movement(Wind).</p>
<p>Leucorrhea- This occurs mainly due to hyperplasia of vaginal epithelial cells and also due to cervical changes as a result of increased hormonal levels during pregnancy. It can also be as a result of vaginal infection or vaginal irritants.</p>
<p>8 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>b) Probable signs.</p>
<p>These are signs that are highly suggestive of pregnancy however they are not specific(definitive) to pregnancy.</p>
<p>They are signs obtained from physical examination.</p>
<p>These signs include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Enlargement of the uterus to become globular in shape. This sign might also be as a result of uterine tumours.</li>
<li>Cervix become soft (Hegar's or Goodell's sign or Ladin's sign) â€“ on bimanual examination, a firm cervix is felt softer body and compressible, softer isthmus at about 6 -8 weeks. Although this sign is associated with pregnancy, it may also occur in pelvic congestion.</li>
<li>Darkening of the vaginal mucosa from 8 weeks. It reaches maximum intensity at the 16th week and then persists throughout pregnancy. Also known as Chadwick's sign or Jacquemier's sign which is the dark purplish/bluish colour and congestion of the vulva and vaginal mucous membranes.</li>
<li>Pulsation in fornices (Osiander's sign). When this is due to pregnancy, it occurs at around 8 weeks. However this can also be found in pelvic congestion.</li>
<li>Immunological test in which the HcG secreted by the blastocyst is found in the woman's early morning urine/ blood specimen as early as 2 weeks gestation. HcG is also found in women with Choriocarcinoma and Hydatidiform mole hence making this test not specific to pregnancy.</li>
<li>Internal ballotment may be done from 16 weeks but this may be difficult in primigravida and fat women.</li>
<li>Ease in flexibility of the body of uterus (McDonald's sign).</li>
<li>Irregular softening and enlargement of the uterine fundus (Von Fernwald's sign).</li>
<li>Uterine contractions elicited by bimanual examination (Palmer's sign).</li>
<li>Piskacek's sign-This refers to a palpable soft prominence in one of the location where uterine tubes meets the uterus (Cornua).</li>
<li>Early bleeding that may be associated with implantation process (Hartman's sign). This is not a specific sign to pregnancy as it may be as a result of other causes such as tumors and infections of reproductive tract.</li>
<li>Braxton hick's contraction (at 16 weeks)- irregular painless contractions that may be felt upon palpation. They prepare the uterus for labor as well as facilitating circulation of blood to and fro the placenta. However, these may be confused with intestinal movements.</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Positive signs.</p>
<p>These are signs that confirms existence of pregnancy. It means there is no any other alternative diagnosis in presence of these signs. They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Visualization of foetus through Ultrasound or X-ray</li>
<li>Presence of foetal heart sounds through ultrasound or fetoscope</li>
</ul>
<p>9 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Palpable or visible foetal movements</p>
<p>Palpable foetal parts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="estimation-of-gestational-age">Estimation of gestational age<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#estimation-of-gestational-age" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Gestational age can be estimated through: -</p>
<p>Fundal Heightâ€”This is the measurement of foetal growth taken from the pubic bone to the top of the uterus. It is done in centimeters and centimeters are used then used to determine foetal growth in terms of weeks.</p>
<p>Use of LMP to calculate EDD. This method is referred to as Naegeleâ€™s Rule or Naegeleâ€™s Formula. In this, you take the first day of normal last menstrual period, add 7 to the dates and 9 to the months. However, this method is based on a normal 28 daysâ€™ menstrual cycle. For example, if the LMP is 12/01/2020 then EDD would be 19/10/2020.</p>
<p>Use of radiological tests such as Ultrasound or X-rays.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiological-changes-of-pregnancy-and-minor-disorders-in-pregnancy">Physiological Changes of Pregnancy and Minor disorders in pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiological-changes-of-pregnancy-and-minor-disorders-in-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of the lesson the student will be able to;</p>
<p>a) Describe the physiological changes that mimic or mask pregnancy.</p>
<p>b) Explain minor disorders associated with pregnancy and their management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are physiological biochemical and anatomical changes that occur during pregnancy. These changes may be systemic or local.</p>
<p>Most of the systemic changes return to pre pregnancy status 6 weeks after delivery. These changes occur during pregnancy to maintain a healthy environment for the fetus without compromising the motherâ€™s health as well as preparing for the process of delivery and care of the newborn.</p>
<p>Understanding of the normal changes helps to understand coincidental disease processes.</p>
<p>Pregnancy is a critical period for both the woman and her unborn child. It is, therefore, very important for you to understand the physiological changes that occur during pregnancy in order to appreciate the effect they may have on the pregnant woman and to be able to manage her pregnancy appropriately.</p>
<p>10 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>This topic will discuss changes in the following systems and organs:</p>
<p>a) The reproductive organs
b) The cardiovascular system
c) The respiratory system
d) The renal system
e) The gastrointestinal system
f) Maternal weight
g) Musculoskeletal system
h) The skin</p>
<ol>
<li>Changes in the Reproductive Organs</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Changes in the Uterus</p>
<p>The uterine muscle fibre increases in size (hypertrophy) and in number (hyperplasia). The uterus continues to grow this way for the first 20 weeks, thereafter, it stretches to accommodate its contents. It increases in size from 60 grams - 900 grams.</p>
<p>By the eighth week of gestation it begins to generate small waves of contractions known as Braxton Hicks contractions, which are painless and continue throughout pregnancy. The blood supply to the uterus increases to keep pace with its growth and also to meet the needs of the placenta.</p>
<p>In early pregnancy the uterus becomes globular in shape to accommodate the fetal growth, liquor, amnii and placental tissue. This causes pressure on other pelvic organs.</p>
<p>Uterus â€“ Upper part fundus and body change in to upper uterine segment</p>
<p>b) Changes in the Cervix</p>
<p>The cervix acts as an effective barrier against infection. It also protects the pregnancy.</p>
<p>Under the influence of progesterone, the endo-cervical cells secrete mucus, which becomes a cervical plug known as operculum.</p>
<p>This plug provides protection from ascending infection. In late pregnancy, the cervix softens in response to increasing painless contractions.</p>
<p>Prostaglandins are thought to have a role in cervical softening in readiness for the onset of labour. Lower part cervix and isthmus change in to lower uterine segment</p>
<p>c) Changes in the Vagina</p>
<p>Estrogen causes the vagina to become more elastic. These changes will allow dilatation during the second stage of labour to receive the descending fetal head.</p>
<p>There is an increased amount of the normal white vaginal discharge called leucorrhoea.</p>
<p>11 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>The vaginal PH becomes more acidic to provide protection to some micro-organisms but also increases susceptibility to others such as candida albicans.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-changes-in-the-cardiovascular-system">2. Changes in the Cardiovascular System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-changes-in-the-cardiovascular-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-position-and-size-of-heart">a) Position and Size of Heart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-position-and-size-of-heart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>As the uterus enlarges and the diaphragm becomes elevated the heart is displaced upward and somewhat to the left with rotation on its long axis, so that the apex beat is moved laterally.</p>
<p>Cardiac capacity increases by 70-80mL; this may be due to increased volume or hypertrophy of cardiac muscle. The size of the heart appears to increase by about 12%</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-cardiac-output">b) Cardiac Output<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-cardiac-output" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Cardiac output increases approximately 40% during pregnancy, reaching its maximum at 20-24 weeks gestation and continuing at this level until term.</p>
<p>The increase in output can be as much as 1.5L/min over the non pregnant level and is higher in multiple pregnancy.</p>
<p>The cardiac output increases from 5L to 7L/min by late pregnancy. This is caused by an increase in resting heart rate of about 15 beats per minute by the end of pregnancy and an increase in blood volume.</p>
<p>Cardiac output is very sensitive to changes in body position. This sensitivity increases with advancing gestation.</p>
<p>In a pregnant woman lying flat on her back, the uterus impinges upon the inferior vena cava, thereby decreasing venous return to the heart leading to supine hypotension syndrome.</p>
<p>Clients in advanced pregnancy are therefore discouraged from lying in this position.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-blood-pressure">c) Blood Pressure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-blood-pressure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Systemic blood pressure declines slightly during pregnancy. There is a little change in systolic blood pressure, but diastolic pressure is reduced (5-10mmHg) from about 12-26 weeks.</p>
<p>Diastolic pressure increases thereafter to pre-pregnancy levels by about 36 weeks. (It is important to know the pre-pregnancy diastolic BP in order to accurately diagnose hypertensive disease in pregnancy).</p>
<p>The elevated venous pressure returns toward normal if the woman lies in the lateral recumbent position.</p>
<p>The obstruction posed by the uterus on the inferior vena cava and the pressure of the fetal presenting part on the common iliac vein can result in decreased venous return to the heart. This</p>
<p>12 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>decreases cardiac output, leads to a fall in blood pressure, and contributes to edema in the lower limbs</p>
<p>d) Venous pressure</p>
<p>There is no change in the upper body but venous return tends to increase in the lower extremities. There is decrease in venous return to the heart increases pressure and this results in edema.</p>
<p>e) Peripheral Resistance.</p>
<p>Peripheral resistance declines because of decreased blood pressure and increased cardiac output. The red cell mass increases by about 18% by the end of the pregnancy. The plasma volume increases from the 10th week of pregnancy and reaches its maximum level of 50% above non-pregnant values by the 32nd to 34th week, and maintains this until term.</p>
<p>As the plasma increase is greater than that of the red cell mass, there is hemo-dilution effect. This results in lowered hemoglobin level. This effect is referred to as physiological anemia. The mean acceptable HB level in pregnancy is 10 - 12 g/dl of blood.</p>
<p>f) Effects of the Labour on the Cardiovascular System</p>
<p>When a patient is in supine position, uterine contractions can cause a 25% increase in maternal cardiac output, a 15% decrease in heart rate, and a resultant 33% increase in stroke volume.</p>
<p>However when the laboring patient is in the lateral recumbent position, the hemodynamic parameters stabilize, with only a 7.6% increase in cardiac output, a 0.7% decrease in heart rate, and a 7.7% increase in stroke volume.</p>
<p>These significant differences are attributable to inferior vena cava occlusion caused by the gravid uterus.</p>
<p>During contractions, pulse pressure increases 26% in the supine position but only 6% in the lateral recumbent position.</p>
<p>Central venous pressure increases in direct relationship to the intensity of uterine contraction and increased intra-abdominal pressure.</p>
<p>Additionally, cardiopulmonary blood volume increases 300-500mL during contractions. At the time of delivery, hemodynamic alterations vary with the anesthetic used.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Changes in the Respiratory System</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Anatomic and Physiologic Changes</p>
<p>Pregnancy produces anatomic and physiologic changes that affect respiratory performance. Early in pregnancy, capillary dilatation occurs throughout the respiratory tract, leading to engorgement of the nasopharynx, larynx, trachea and bronchi.</p>
<p>13 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>This causes the voice to change and makes breathing though the nose difficult. Respiratory infections and preeclampsia aggravate these symptoms. Chest X-rays reveal increased vascular makings in the lungs.</p>
<p>As the uterus enlarges, the diaphragm is elevated as much as 4cm, and the rib cage is displaced upward and widens, increasing the lower thoracic diameter by 2cm and the thoracic circumference by up to 6cm.</p>
<p>Elevation of the diaphragm does not impede its movement. Abdominal muscles have less tone and are less active during the pregnancy, causing respiration to be mainly diaphragmatic.</p>
<p>b) Volumes and Capacities</p>
<p>Alterations occurring in lung volumes and capacities during pregnancy include the following:</p>
<p>i. Dead volume increases owing to relaxation of the musculature of conducting airways.
ii. Tidal volume increases gradually (35-50%) as pregnancy progresses. Total lung capacity is reduced (4-5%) by the elevation of the diaphragm.
iii. Functional residual capacity, residual volume, and respiratory reserve volume all decrease by about 20%.
iv. Functional respiratory changes include a slight increase in respiratory rate, a 50% increase in minute ventilation, a 40% increase in tidal volume, and a progressive increase in oxygen consumption of up to 15-20% above non pregnant levels by term. With the increase in respiratory tidal volume associated with a normal respiratory rate, there is an increase in respiratory minute volume of approximately 26%.
v. Larger tidal volume and smaller residual volume cause increased alveolar ventilation (about 65%) during pregnancy. Inspiratory capacity increases by 5-10%.
vi. As the respiratory minute volume increases, â€œhyperventilation of pregnancy â€œoccurs, causing a decrease in alveolar CO2.
vii. This decrease lowers the maternal blood CO2 tension; however alveolar oxygen tension is maintained within normal limits.
viii. Maternal hyperventilation is considered a protective measure that prevents the fetus from the exposure to excessive levels of CO2.</p>
<p>c) Effects of Labour on the Pulmonary System</p>
<p>There is a further decrease in functional residual capacity (FRC) during the early phase of each uterine contraction, resulting from redistribution of blood from the uterus to the central venous pool.</p>
<p>14 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Because this decrease in functional residual capacity (FRC) occurs without a concomitant change in dead space, there is little residual dilution and, therefore, presumably more efficient gas exchange.</p>
<p>Capillary dilatation occurs in the respiratory route (Nasopharynx, larynx, trachea, bronchi) and this make breathing difficult through nose, enlarged Uterus pushes the diaphragm and the lungs as well.</p>
<p>d) Summary of Pulmonary changes</p>
<p>i. Changes to volume
ii. Tidal volume increase by 35-50%
iii. Residual volume decreased by 20%
iv. Expiratory reserve volume decrease by 20%
v. So increase Tidal volume and decrease Residual volume leading to increased alveolar ventilation by 65%.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Changes in the Gastrointestinal Tract</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Introduction.</p>
<p>There is increased salivation. Women often experience changes in their sense of taste, leading to dietary changes and food cravings. Craving for substances such as bricks/soil is known as pica.</p>
<p>Excessive secretion of saliva during pregnancy is called ptyalism gravidarum.</p>
<p>Progesterone relaxes the smooth muscles. Gastric emptying and peristalsis are reduced in order to maximize the absorption of nutrients. Heartburn is common and is associated with gastric reflux due to relaxation of the cardiac sphincter.</p>
<p>Constipation is also common due to sluggish gut motility. Nausea and vomiting occur mainly during early pregnancy as a result of raised hormonal levels.</p>
<p>As the fetus and placenta grow and place increasing demands on the mother, phenomenal alterations in metabolism occur. The most obvious physical changes are weight gain and altered body shape.</p>
<p>Weight gain is due not only to the uterus and its contents but also to increase breast tissue, blood and water volume in the form of extra vascular and extracellular fluid.</p>
<p>Deposition of fat and protein and increased cellular water are added to the maternal stores.</p>
<p>The expected weight gain is approximately 2kg in the first 20 weeks followed by an average of 0.5 kg per week until term leading to 12 kg in total.</p>
<p>During normal pregnancy, approximately 1000g of weight gain is attributable to protein. Half of this is found in the fetus and the placenta, with the rest being distributed as uterine contractile protein, breast glandular tissue, plasma protein, and hemoglobin.</p>
<p>Total body fat increases during pregnancy, but the amount varies with total weight gain.</p>
<p>15 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>During the second half of pregnancy, plasma lipids increase, but triglycerides, cholesterol and lipoproteins decrease soon after delivery.</p>
<p>The ratio of low density lipoproteins to high density lipoproteins increases during pregnancy.</p>
<p>b) Oral Cavity:</p>
<p>Salivation may seem to increase due to difficulty in swallowing associated with nausea. This is prevalent mainly in the first trimester and should reduce with time.</p>
<p>Tooth decay during pregnancy, is not due to lack of calcium in the teeth. Indeed, dental calcium is stable and not mobilized during pregnancy as is bone calcium. If the pH of the oral cavity increases, tooth decay may occur. Pregnant women are therefore encouraged to maintain good oral hygiene.</p>
<p>The gums may become hypertrophic hyperaemic and friable; this maybe due to increased systemic estrogen. Vitamin C deficiency can also cause tenderness and bleeding of the gums. The gums should return to normal in the early puerperium</p>
<p>Gums becomes hypertrophic and hyperemic easily bleed (20 to increased systemic estrogen)</p>
<p>Gastrointestinal mobility May be reduced due to increased progesterone (w/c decreased the hormone motilin stimulate smooth muscles in GII) hence gastric emptying is slowed.</p>
<p>Similarly, in other part of GIT constipation (due to increased water absorption) Stomach Production of gastrin increase increased gastric volume and decreases PH, mucous production increased</p>
<p>c) Gastrointestinal Motility</p>
<p>Gastrointestinal motility may be reduced during pregnancy due to increased levels of progesterone, which in turn decrease the production of motilin, a hormonal peptide that is known to stimulate smooth muscle in the gut.</p>
<p>This leads to a feeling of bloatedness which is common among pregnant women. Transit time of food throughout the gastrointestinal tract may be so much slower that more water than normal is reabsorbed, leading to constipation.</p>
<p>d) Stomach and esophagus</p>
<p>Gastric production of hydrochloric acid may be increased leading to hyperacidity (heart burn).</p>
<p>Esophageal peristalsis is decreased, accompanied by gastric reflux because of the slower emptying time and dilatation or relaxation of the gastro- esophageal sphincter.</p>
<p>Gastric reflux is more prevalent in later pregnancy owing to elevation of the stomach by the enlarged uterus.</p>
<p>These alterations as well as lying in the supine position, make the use of anesthesia more hazardous because of the increased possibility of regurgitation and aspiration.</p>
<p>16 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>e) Small and Large Bowel and Appendix</p>
<p>During pregnancy, the large and small bowels are displaced upward and laterally, the appendix is displaced superiorly in the right flank area.</p>
<p>These organs return to the normal positions in the early puerperium. As noted previously, motility and gastrointestinal tone are decreased.</p>
<p>f) Gallbladder</p>
<p>Gallbladder function is also altered during pregnancy because of the hypotonia of the smooth muscle wall.</p>
<p>Emptying time is slowed and often incomplete. Progesterone decreased motility leading to decreased empting time of bile hence causing stasis predisposing pregnant women to stone formation and infection.</p>
<p>Bile can become thick, and bile stasis may lead to gallstone formation.</p>
<p>g) Liver</p>
<p>There are no apparent morphologic changes in the liver during normal pregnancy, but there are functional alterations.</p>
<p>Serum alkaline phosphatase activity can double, probably because of increased placental alkaline phosphatase isoenzymes.</p>
<p>Thus, a decrease in the albumin/globulin ratio occurs normally in pregnancy. This needs to be taken into consideration when interpreting LFT results.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Kidneys and Urinary Tract</li>
</ol>
<p>Progesterone relaxes the walls of the ureters and allows dilation and kinking. This tends to result in a slowing down or stasis of urinary flow, making infection a greater possibility.</p>
<p>a) Renal Dilatation.</p>
<p>During pregnancy, each kidney increases in length by 1-1.5cm, with a concomitant increase in weight. The renal pelvis usually dilates. The ureters dilate, elongate, widen, and become more curved. Thus there is an increase in urinary stasis; this may lead to infection and may make tests of renal function difficult to interpret.</p>
<p>b) Renal Function</p>
<p>The glomerular filtration rate (GFR) increases during pregnancy by about 50%. The renal plasma flow rate increases by as much as 25-50%. Urinary flow and sodium excretion rates in late pregnancy can be altered by posture, being twice as great in the lateral recumbent position as in the supine position.</p>
<p>17 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Even though the GFR increases dramatically during pregnancy, the volume of the urine passed each day does not increase. Consequently, the serum urea and creatinine levels are reduced.</p>
<p>The increase in GFR coupled with the impairment of tubular reabsorption capacity for filtered glucose leads to glycosuria. Increased levels of urinary glucose also contribute to increased susceptibility to urinary tract infection (UTI).</p>
<p>Normally there is little change in Proteinuria during pregnancy; and therefore if more than 500mg/24h is lost, a disease process should be suspected e.g. pre-eclampsia/ eclampsia.</p>
<p>Renal function Change occur due to increased maternal and placental hormones (ACTH, ADH, cortisole, etc.) and increase in plasma volume.</p>
<p>Glomerular Filtration Rate increase by 50% (begins early and last up to term)</p>
<p>Renal blood flow rate increase by 20-25% (early to midtrimester) after the end of 2nd trimester remain constant.</p>
<p>Urine volume dose not increase although glomerular filtration rate increase because of reabsorption.</p>
<p>Creatinine and BUN decrease because of increased clearance rate</p>
<p>Proteinuria shows little changes during pregnancy.</p>
<p>c) Water Retention</p>
<p>Fluid retention, swelling or 'edema' affects about 65% of healthy pregnant women with a normal blood pressure.</p>
<p>While it can occur at any time in the pregnancy, it more commonly happens in the last 3 months of the pregnancy.</p>
<p>This is because by about 32 weeks, the blood circulating in the woman's body has increased by up to 50%.</p>
<p>It typically involves the lower extremities but occasionally appears as swelling or puffiness in the face or hands.</p>
<p>d) Edema.</p>
<p>The most common cause of edema in pregnancy is Physiologic edema. This is due to an increase in the total amount of body fluid and a lower concentration of protein to keep the fluid in the blood vessels.</p>
<p>It may also result from hormone-induced sodium retention.</p>
<p>Pedal edema may also occur when the enlarged uterus intermittently compresses the inferior vena cava during recumbency, obstructing outflow from both femoral veins.</p>
<p>18 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Physiological edema is a diagnosis of exclusion. (Physical examination aims to rule out the pathologic causes). Physiologic edema tends to worsen during the day especially when the patient is ambulant.</p>
<p>It is reduced by lying in the left lateral decubitus position, elevating the lower extremities, and using compression stockings. Pathological edema on the other hand, usually persists, even after elevating the feet.</p>
<p>Pathological causes of edema are less common but often dangerous. They include deep venous thrombosis (DVT), preeclampsia, renal disease and cardiac disease in pregnancy. Extensive, cellulitis, which usually causes focal erythema, may resemble general edema.</p>
<p>e) Bladder</p>
<p>As the uterus enlarges; the urinary bladder is displaced upward and is flattened in the anterior-posterior diameter.</p>
<p>Bladder vascularity increases and muscle tone decreases, thereby increasing its capacity up to 1500ml.</p>
<p>Pressure from the uterus leads to increase in urinary frequency. This effect increases as pregnancy advances.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Hematologic System</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Blood Volume</p>
<p>The blood volume increases progressively until term by about 45-50% and is higher in multiple pregnancies.</p>
<p>The reason for increase in blood volume are:</p>
<p>i. More blood is required for extra blood flow to the uterus.
ii. Need for extra metabolic needs of fetus and the mother.
iii. Increased perfusion of other organs, especially kidneys.
iv. The increased volume also compensates for maternal blood loss during delivery.</p>
<p>b) Red Blood Cells</p>
<p>The red blood cell mass increases by about 33%, however the plasma volume increases earlier and faster than red blood cell volume. This leads to physiologic anemia in pregnancy.</p>
<p>The hematocrit (PCV) then stabilizes or may increase slightly near term.</p>
<p>c) Iron</p>
<p>With the increase in red blood cells, the need for iron for the production of hemoglobin naturally increases. If supplemental iron is not added to the diet, iron deficiency anemia will result.</p>
<p>19 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Maternal requirements can reach 5-6mg/d in the latter half of pregnancy. If iron is not readily available, the fetus uses iron from maternal stores.</p>
<p>Thus, the production of fetal hemoglobin is usually adequate even if the mother is severely iron deficient; and therefore anemia in the newborn is rarely a problem.</p>
<p>Instead, maternal iron deficiency more commonly may cause preterm labour and late spontaneous abortion, increasing the incidence of fetal wastage and maternal morbidity.</p>
<p>d) White Blood Cells</p>
<p>The total blood leukocyte counts increases during pregnancy from a pre-pregnancy level of 4300-4500/ml to 5000-12000/ml in the last trimester.</p>
<p>The polymorphonuclear leucocytes are the main contributors to this increase.</p>
<p>Lymphocyte and monocyte numbers stay essentially the same throughout pregnancy.</p>
<p>This should be taken into account when interpreting results of WBC counts in pregnancy.</p>
<p>e) Clotting Factors</p>
<p>During pregnancy, levels of several essential coagulation factors increase. There are marked increases in fibrinogen and factor VIII. Factors VII, IX, X, and XII also increased but to a lesser extent.</p>
<p>There is a decrease in factors- XI and XIII</p>
<p>Fibrinolytic activity is depressed during pregnancy and labour, although the precise mechanism is unknown.</p>
<p>Plasminogen levels increase concomitantly with fibrinogens levels, causing equilibrium of clotting and lysing activity.</p>
<p>Understanding these physiologic changes is necessary to manage two of the more serious problems of pregnancy â€“ (that is hemorrhage and thromboembolic disease both caused by disorders in the mechanism of hemostasis).</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Changes in the Breast</li>
</ol>
<p>Breast increases in size with enlargement of the nipple and increased vascularity and pigmentation of areola.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Change in Skin</li>
</ol>
<p>Hyperpigmentation over some part of the body Face (forehead, cheek) known as chloasma</p>
<p>In the abdomen the sub-umbilical midline dark purplish pigmentation known as linea nigra</p>
<p>There is development of Stretch marks called Striae gravidarum</p>
<p>There is also Enlargement of abdomen as a result of stretch on collagen fibers of the skin and effect of ACTH.</p>
<p>20 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="minor-disorders-of-pregnancy">MINOR DISORDERS OF PREGNANCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#minor-disorders-of-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Minor disorders are only disorders that occur during pregnancy and are not life threatening.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-digestive-system">1. Digestive system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-digestive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Nausea and vomiting</p>
<p>This presents between 4 and 12 weeksâ€™ gestation. Hormonal influences are listed as the most likely causes this are HCG, oestrogen and progesterone. It is usually occurring in the morning but can occur any time during the day, aggravated by smelling of food.</p>
<p><strong>Management:</strong></p>
<p>i. Reassure the mother
ii. Small frequent meals (dry meals)
iii. Reduce fatty and fried containing foods.
iv. Rest
v. Eat small meals frequently, every two to three hours; do not skip meals; avoid hunger.
vi. Have a snack before bedtime or during the night.
vii. Try eating a piece of bread or a few crackers before getting up in the morning to quell nausea.
viii. Get out of bed slowly; avoid sudden movements.
ix. Avoid high fat and fried foods; eat lower-fat meats, poultry and fish; use skim or low-fat milk products; try carbohydrate-rich foods such as fruit, fruit juice, breads, cereals, rice, potatoes.
x. Drink fluids between rather than with meals to avoid stomach fullness at meal times.
xi. Avoid strong food smells and cooking odours by eating cold foods, opening windows to freshen the air, avoiding coffee, garlic and other spices and having others cook when possible.
xii. Avoid highly seasoned foods.
xiii. Avoid brushing your teeth immediately after eating; avoid brushing your tongue.
xiv. Keep well rested; avoid fatigue.
xv. Avoid cigarette smoking.</p>
<p>b) Heartburn:</p>
<p>It is a burning sensation in the mid chest region. Progesterone relaxes the cardiac sphincter of the stomach and allows reflex of gastric contents into esophagus. Heart burn is most troublesome at 30-40 weeks gestation because at this stage is under pressure from the growing uterus.</p>
<p>Relief from heartburn is often achieved through simple dietary and lifestyle changes.</p>
<p><strong>Management:</strong></p>
<p>i. Eat small, lower-fat meals frequently. Dietary fat lowers the oesophageal sphincter tone, already reduced or relaxed by the hormonal changes associated with pregnancy.
ii. Eat slowly, chew food well, avoid tension while eating
iii. Drink fluids between meals rather than with meals to avoid stomach fullness
iv. Avoid spicy foods that seem to exacerbate heartburn</p>
<p>21 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>v. Avoid lying down for at least one to two hours after eating to minimize reflux
vi. Elevate the head of the bed
vii. Avoid bending and stooping after eating
viii. Avoid eating and drinking, except for water, before bedtime
ix. Wear loose-fitting clothing
x. Do not take antacids without consulting a physician</p>
<p>c) Excessive Salivation (pytalism)
Occurs from the 8th week of gestation and is thought to be caused by hormones of pregnancy</p>
<p>d) Pica:
This is the term used when mother craves certain foods of unnatural substances such as coal, soil...etc. The cause is unknown but hormones and changes in metabolism are blamed.</p>
<p>Management:
i. Seek medical advice if the substance craved is potentially harmful to the unborn baby.
ii. Ask pregnant women if they have cravings for non-food items such as dirt or clay.
iii. Advice women you suspect may be eating non-food substances of the potential risks.
iv. If the behaviour persists, monitor iron status, maternal health and foetal development carefully.</p>
<p>e) Constipation
Constipation affects 11 to 38 percent of pregnant women. Constipation during pregnancy is linked to several physiological changes associated with pregnancy as well as an eating pattern low in fibre and liquids.</p>
<p>Hormonal changes relax the gastrointestinal tract, decreasing motility and increasing the transit time of waste through the colon.</p>
<p>Increases in progesterone levels also promote increased absorption of water from the colon, a factor linked to constipation.</p>
<p>The enlarging uterus contributes to constipation by putting pressure on the colon, sometimes displacing it and making bowel movements more difficult. Decreased physical activity, extra bed rest and iron supplements may also contribute to this common discomfort. Dietary and lifestyle changes usually correct it.</p>
<p>Management:
i. Increase the intake of water, fresh fruit, vegetables and ruphages in the diet
ii. Exercise is helpful especially walking
iii. Increase fibre intake by eating more whole grain breads and cereals; vegetables; and fruit and legumes such as beans, split peas and lentils.
iv. Drink between 8 and 12 cups of fluid every day in the form of water, milk and juice. Warm or hot fluids may be particularly helpful.
v. Maintain an active lifestyle, for example, by walking or swimming regularly.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>vi. Avoid all laxatives unless one is recommended by a physician. Some types of laxatives are contraindicated during pregnancy.</p>
<p>f) Lack of appetite</p>
<p>This is a common condition in pregnancy which can lead to inadequate intake of food at a time of increased nutrient need.</p>
<p>Management:</p>
<p>i. Eat small frequent meals spaced throughout the day (5-6 meals per day)
ii. Schedule a regular eating time
iii. Eat protein from animal or plant source with snacks and meals whenever possible
iv. Drink plenty of liquids, preferable in between meals
v. Take walks before meals to stimulate appetite
vi. Choose and prepare food that look and smell good for you
vii. Use spices such as onions, garlic, cinnamon, and ginger to stimulate appetite, improve flavour and digestion</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Musculoskeletal system</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Backache</p>
<p>The hormones sometime soften the segments to such a degree that some support is needed.</p>
<p>Management:</p>
<p>i. Advice the mother to sleep on firm bed.
ii. Advice support mechanisms of the back.</p>
<p>b) Muscle cramps</p>
<p>The cause of leg cramps in pregnancy is unknown, it may be due to ischaemia or results from changes in PH or electrolyte status</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>i. Advise to dorsoflex the foot, hold the knees straight and then stretches the calf muscles by pulling the foot upwards while in the sitting position
ii. Alternatively standing firmly on the affected leg and striding forward with the other leg will stretch the calf muscles</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Circulatory system</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Fainting:</p>
<p>In early pregnancy fainting may be due to the vasodilation occurring under the influence of progesterone before there has been a compensatory increase in blood volume. The weight of the uterine contents presses on the inferior venacava and slows the return of blood to the heart.</p>
<p>Management:</p>
<p>i. Avoid long period of standing
ii. Sit or lie down when she feels slight dizziness
iii. She would be wise not to lie on her back except during abdominal examination</p>
<p>b) Varicosities</p>
<p>Progesterone relaxes the smooth muscles of the veins and result in sluggish circulation. The valves of the dilated veins become insufficient and varicosities result. It occurs in legs, anus (hemorrhoids) and vulva.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Management:
i. Exercising the calf muscles by rising on the toes
ii. Elevate the leg and rest on the table
iii. Support thighs and legs
iv. Anal region: Avoid constipation and advise adequate fluid intake.
v. Vulva: Sanitary pad give support for vulva varicosities</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>The nervous system
a) Carpal tunnel syndrome
The mother complains of numbness â€˜pins and needlesâ€™ in her fingers and hands, it usually happens in the morning but it can occur at any time of the day, it is caused by fluid retention which creates edema and pressure of the medial nerve</li>
</ol>
<p>Management
i. Wearing a splint at night with hand resting high on 2 or 3 pillows may bring relief
ii. Reassure her that the condition will resolve after delivery
iii. Sometimes the doctor may prescribe antidiuretics but the conservative approach is more favored
b) Insomnia</p>
<p>Inability to fall asleep or to remain asleep for an adequate length of time</p>
<p>Although it is grouped under minor discomfort, it must never be dismissed lightly, it may be caused by nocturia and the discomfort in bed due to the growing fetus, the increased blood supply to the uterus on lying down sometimes causes the baby to move a lot</p>
<p>Management
i. Reassurance and advice to go to bed early with hope that the fetus being active earlier and sleep after sometime
ii. Talk with the woman about fear and anxiety of pregnancy
iii. Encourage those who can, to sleep in the afternoon when sleep can easily come</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Genitourinary system
a) Frequency of micturition
Occurs in early weeks of pregnancy when the growing fetus is still situated within the pelvis and competes for space required by the bladder, later the problem becomes apparent when the fetal head has entered the pelvis and reduces the space that is available</li>
</ol>
<p>Management
i. After excluding other causes of bladder irritability e.g infection, the midwife need to reassure the mother that it is a short time problem that will be over after 12 weeks, for late pregnancy it will be over after birth
b) Leucorrhea
It is a term used for the increased non-irritant vaginal discharge in pregnancy</p>
<p>Management
i. After excluding infections e.g thrush or trichomonalis then explain to the mother that it is normal, encourage her that she washes her vulva with plain water daily, she should wear cotton under pants and avoid tights.</p>
<p>24 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>NB:
Minor disorders can develop into a more serious complication of pregnancy. In case these disorders deteriorate into more serious disorders immediate and prompt actions should be commenced. (Review on Danger signals of pregnancy as discussed in our previous lessons)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antenatal-care">Antenatal care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antenatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition-of-antenatal-care">Definition of antenatal care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-antenatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Antenatal care (ANC) is health care given to a pregnant woman from the time conception is confirmed to the onset of labour.</p>
<p>The midwife should provide a personalized care approach that is centered on the woman's needs by sharing information with the woman to help her make informed choices.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aim-of-antenatal-care">Aim of antenatal care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim-of-antenatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The main aim of antenatal care is to monitor progress of pregnancy in order to ensure the mother reaches the end of pregnancy both physically and psychologically healthy and that she delivers a healthy baby.</p>
<p>Antenatal care furthers ensures that good obstetrical outcomes are achieved for the mother and baby and prevent any complications that may occur in pregnancy, labour, delivery and the postpartum period</p>
<p>A quality antenatal care should entail: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Accurate Diagnosis of pregnancy.</li>
<li>Regular blood pressure checks, testing for oedema, and urine examination</li>
<li>Regular abdominal examination.</li>
<li>The recognition of high risk cases and their referral for special mothers</li>
<li>Immunization against tetanus to both the mother and unborn baby</li>
<li>Treating of minor complications during pregnancy.</li>
<li>Health education eg. On nutrition, ANC visits, danger signs etc</li>
</ul>
<p>During Antenatal clinic visits, the midwife should: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Ensure that the mother understands the benefits Antenatal Care.</li>
<li>Educate the mother on how to look after herself and her baby (diet, hygiene, e.t.c)</li>
<li>Prepare the mother psychologically and physically for delivery.</li>
<li>Provide prophylactic treatment against anemia and vaccination against tetanus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Identify mothers high risk women who might have problems during pregnancy or labour, and correct the abnormalities or refer to hospital for management of the pregnancy or delivery.</p>
<p>Help a mother to draw an Individual Birth Plan (IBP).</p>
<p>The midwife should also be aware that successful outcomes of pregnancy depends on various factors such as: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Reproductive efficiency of the mother.</li>
<li>The parity of the mother</li>
<li>The age of the mother</li>
<li>Physique and stature of the mother</li>
<li>General health state of the mother</li>
<li>Quality of obstetric care.</li>
</ul>
<p>The midwife should therefore be aware of these factors and should evaluate how they might influence the outcome of pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fanc-focused-antenatal-care">FANC: Focused antenatal care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fanc-focused-antenatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition-of-fanc">Definition of FANC.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-fanc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Focused Antenatal Care is a personalized (individualized) care provided to a pregnant woman which emphasizes on woman's overall health, her preparedness for childbirth and her readiness for complications.</p>
<p>Focused Antenatal Care (or targeted Antenatal care) can also refer to a minimum number of four comprehensive personalized antenatal visits, each of which has specific items of client assessment, education and care to ensure prevention or early detection and prompt management of complications.</p>
<p>FANC categorizes pregnant women into two groups, namely:</p>
<p>a) Those eligible to receive routine antenatal care (Basic component).</p>
<p>b) Those who need special care based on the specific pregnancy related risk factor (High risk pregnancies) such as previous history of still birth, spontaneous miscarriage, low birth weight or macrocosmic baby, hypertension in pregnancy or current pregnancy factors such as multiple pregnancy, Rh- mothers, pelvic abnormalities, per vaginal bleeding and mothers with medical conditions.</p>
<p>Focused Antenatal care should be:</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Timely</p>
<p>Friendly</p>
<p>Simple</p>
<p>Safe</p>
<p>Accessible.</p>
<p>Care provider should be aware that women are more likely to seek and return for services if they feel cared for and respected. This therefore requires that care providers should use excellent interpersonal skills and should respect clients' right to dignity, privacy, confidentiality, full and accurate information.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim-of-focused-antenatal-care">Aim of Focused Antenatal Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim-of-focused-antenatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The aim of Focused Antenatal Care is to achieve a good outcome for the mother and baby and prevent any complications that may occur in pregnancy, labour, delivery and post-partum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives-of-focused-antenatal-fanc">Objectives of focused antenatal (FANC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-focused-antenatal-fanc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives-of-fanc-are">Objectives of FANC are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-fanc-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Early detection and treatment of problems
ii. Prevention of complications using safe, simple and cost-effective interventions
iii. Birth preparedness and complication readiness
iv. Health promotion using health messages and counseling
v. Provision of care by a skilled attendant</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-detection-and-treatment-of-problems">Early detection and treatment of problems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-detection-and-treatment-of-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health care providers should aim at detecting and preventing health problems such as severe anemia, per vaginal bleeding, malaria, TB, STIs, Decreased or absent foetal movement, etc.</p>
<p>Every pregnancy should be considered as a risky pregnancy and every pregnant woman should be prepared for the possibility of complications.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-complications-using-safe-simple-and-cost-effective-interventions">Prevention of complications using safe, simple and cost-effective interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-complications-using-safe-simple-and-cost-effective-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Service providers should ensure prevention of complications. This can be achieved through preventive services such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus Toxoid to prevent maternal and neonatal tetanus</li>
<li>Iron/Folate (IFAS) supplementation to prevent anemia and foetal malformations.</li>
<li>Use of IPT and LLITNs to prevent malaria/anemia.</li>
<li>Environmental hygiene to prevent intestinal worms.</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Use of Mebendazole after first trimester to prevent intestinal worms</p>
<p>Cessation of smoking and drug use during pregnancy.</p>
<p>Proper nutrition during pregnancy.</p>
<p>Elimination of mother to child transmission of HIV(eMTCT).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="national-guidelines-for-tetanus-toxoid">National guidelines for Tetanus Toxoid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-guidelines-for-tetanus-toxoid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Dose of TT</th><th>When to give</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td>At first contact or as early as possible in pregnancy</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>At least 4 weeks after TT1</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>At least 6 months after TT2 or during subsequent pregnancy</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>At least 1 year after TT3 or during subsequent pregnancy</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>At least 1 year after TT4 or during subsequent pregnancy</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Birth preparedness and complication readiness.</p>
<p>Health care provider need to discuss components of an individualized birth plan(IBP) with the woman and assist her to draw one. Components of Individualized birth plan includes: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Place of birth</li>
<li>Emergency funds</li>
<li>Birth companion</li>
<li>Transportation</li>
<li>Decision maker</li>
<li>Skilled attendant</li>
<li>Blood donor</li>
<li>Knowledge on danger signs</li>
<li>Accurate calculation of EDD</li>
</ul>
<p>Health promotion using health messages and counseling.</p>
<p>Service provider should use health messages to promote the following: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Proper nutrition</li>
<li>Rest and hygiene</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Use of IPT and LLITNs</p>
<p>Drug compliance</p>
<p>Safe sex</p>
<p>Family planning and spacing of pregnancy.</p>
<p>Early and exclusive breast feeding.</p>
<p>Newborn care.</p>
<p>Provision of care by a skilled attendant.</p>
<p>A skilled birth attendant refers to a health professional (such as midwife, doctor, clinical officer or a nurse) who has been educated and trained to proficiency in the skills needed to manage pregnancies, child birth and immediate post-natal period and should be able to identify, manage and refer women and newborns with complications.</p>
<p>FANC provides an opportunity to increase skilled care.</p>
<p>Element of Focused Antenatal Care(FANC).</p>
<p>Elements (Components) of FANC are: -</p>
<p>a) History taking
b) Physical examination
c) Health promotion (Through health education and counselling)
d) Provision of preventive services
e) Early detection and treatment of problems
f) Birth preparedness and emergency preparedness.
g) Counselling on danger signs
h) Skilled birth attendant
i) ANC profile
j) Partner(Male) involvement.</p>
<p>FANC Schedule of Visits</p>
<ul>
<li>It is recommended that the pregnant woman should attend a minimum of four comprehensive personalized antenatal visits spread out during the entire pregnancy during which specific focused activities are carried out. The FANC schedule is as follows: -</li>
</ul>
<p>a) First visit less than 16 weeks
b) Second visit 16 - 28 weeks
c) Third visit 28-32 weeks
d) Fourth visit 32 - 40 weeks</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<ul>
<li>NB: Depending on individual need, some women will require additional visits.</li>
</ul>
<p>The first visit</p>
<ul>
<li>The first FANC visit should take place as early as possible, if possible during the first trimester. This visit provides the midwife with an opportunity to obtain baseline data such as weight, blood pressure etc. These baseline data are important because they form a basis for comparison during subsequent visits.</li>
</ul>
<p>Specific activities of the first FANC visit include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Registration</li>
<li>Height and weight measurement</li>
<li>History taking</li>
<li>Physical examination</li>
<li>Laboratory examination (ANC Profile)</li>
<li>Management of complaints</li>
<li>Immunization</li>
<li>Health Education</li>
<li>Advice on Individualized Birth Plan</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Obtain information on:</p>
<p>Personal history</p>
<ul>
<li>Name</li>
<li>Age (date of birth)</li>
<li>Physical address and telephone number</li>
<li>Marital status</li>
<li>Educational level: primary, secondary, university</li>
<li>Economic resources: employed? Type of work, position of patient and husband/guardian</li>
<li>Tobacco use (smoking or chewing habit) or use of other harmful substances?</li>
</ul>
<p>History of present (Current)pregnancy /Present obstetric history.</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain information on date of last menstrual period (LMP). Focus on the certainty of dates, that is, by regularity, accuracy of recall and other relevant information including contraceptive history.</li>
<li>Accurately determine the expected date of delivery(EDD) based on LMP and all other relevant information. EDD can be calculated by adding seven days to the first day of the last normal menstrual period and subtracting three months from that month. For example,</li>
</ul>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES -RUGENDO</p>
<p>if her last period started on 18th June, 18 plus 7 gives you 25. Then June minus three months, (6-3) will give March. So the EDD is March 25th of the following year.</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain information on quickening if applicable.</li>
<li>Check for any associated complication (pain, vaginal bleeding, calf muscle pain)</li>
<li>Social habits: smoking/chewing tobacco, alcohol, drugs (frequency and quantity)</li>
</ul>
<p>Previous Obstetric history.</p>
<ul>
<li>Number of previous pregnancies (Gravida and Parity)</li>
<li>Date (month, year) and outcome of each event (live birth, stillbirth, neonatal death, abortion, ectopic, hydatidiform mole)</li>
<li>Number of ANC attendance.</li>
<li>Type of deliveries</li>
<li>Duration of labour.</li>
<li>Birth weight.</li>
<li>Sex</li>
<li>Puerperium</li>
<li>Specify type and gestation of any abortion, and management if possible (MVA, D&amp;C)</li>
<li>Birth weight of previous pregnancies (if known)</li>
<li>Periods of exclusive breast-feeding: when? For how long?</li>
<li>Special maternal complications and events in previous pregnancies; Specify which pregnancy, validate by records (if possible), Recurrent early abortion, Induced abortion and any associated complications, Thrombosis, Embolus, Breech Or Transverse Presentation. Take history on any Obstetrical operations: Caesarean section (indication, if known), Forceps or vacuum extraction, Manual removal of the placenta, Destructive procedures (craniotomy, decapitation). Also obtain information on: twins pregnancy, low birth weight: &lt;2500g, intrauterine growth restriction, Rhesus-antibody (hydrops), malformed or chromosomally abnormal child, macrocosmic (&gt;4500g) newborn, resuscitation or other treatment of newborn, perinatal, neonatal or infant death (also: later death).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-surgical-history">Medical-Surgical history<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-surgical-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Specific diseases and conditions: tuberculosis, heart disease, chronic renal disease, epilepsy, diabetes mellitus, RTIs, HIV status, if known</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
