<p>Other specific conditions depending on prevalence in the region, e.g. hepatitis, malaria, sickle cell trait</p>
<p>Operations other than caesarean section</p>
<p>Blood transfusions</p>
<p>Rhesus D negative antibodies</p>
<p>Current use of medicines: specify</p>
<p>Period of infertility: when? duration, cause(s)</p>
<ul>
<li>Any other diseases, past or chronic; allergy</li>
</ul>
<p>Gynecological History.</p>
<p>Obtain information relating to menarche, menstrual history, gynecological disorders, reproductive tract infections etc</p>
<p>Family Planning History.</p>
<p>Inquire on previous use of contraception if any, frequency, duration of use, reason for stopping etc</p>
<p>Family History.</p>
<p>On this part, obtain information on any known hereditary condition in the family, significant illness in the family such as diabetes.</p>
<p>Social History</p>
<p>Obtain data on occupation, diet, exercise, smoking, alcohol, marital status, level of education etc</p>
<p>b) Perform physical examination</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A thorough examination is made at the first visit. This is divided into a general examination and an obstetric examination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The aims of physical examination on a pregnant woman is to:-</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>a) To diagnose pregnancy
b) To identify high risk pregnancy
c) To give advice for pregnant mother</p>
<ul>
<li>The general examination should include:</li>
</ul>
<p>General appearance, namely the nutritional status, whether weak or sick looking. Note the gait and if she walks with a limp.</p>
<p>Height, noting that any woman below 150cms in height is likely to have cephalopelvic disproportion.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Weight, that is, a pregnant woman on average gains 2kg every month. The total weight gain by the end of pregnancy is about 10-20kg. Excessive weight gain indicates accumulation of fluid in the tissues (oedema). Lack of increase in weight or loss may mean malnutrition. Obesity may lead to an increased risk of gestational diabetes.</p>
<p>Blood pressure, which is taken in order to ascertain the normal and provide a baseline for comparison. A pressure of 140/90mm/Hg at booking is indicative of hypertension and could cause damage to the placenta.</p>
<p>Pulse, temperature</p>
<p>Signs of anaemia in conjunctiva, hands and tongue pale complexion, fingernails, conjunctiva, oral mucosa, tip of tongue and shortness of breath</p>
<p>Check for oedema of face, hands and ankles</p>
<p>Observe type of breathing and chest generally for abnormalities</p>
<p>FGM status: - If type III discuss the possibility of de-infubulation (opening up either antenatal or during labour)</p>
<p>Varicosities, warts, discharge</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="breast-examination">Breast Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breast-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Palpate gently with the flat of the hand to feel for any lumps.</li>
<li>Check if the nipple is protractile.</li>
<li>Educate the woman on how to examine the breasts by herself.</li>
<li>For further reference on breast examination, refer to Nursing Council Procedure Manual</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="abdominal-examination">Abdominal Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abdominal-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An abdominal examination on a pregnant woman aims at:</p>
<ol>
<li>Observing for signs of pregnancy</li>
<li>Assessing foetal size and growth</li>
<li>Assessing foetal health</li>
<li>Diagnosing the location of foetal parts</li>
<li>Detecting any deviation from normal</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-for-abdominal-examination">Steps for Abdominal Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-for-abdominal-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Inspection</li>
<li>Palpation</li>
<li>Auscultation</li>
</ol>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Inspection (5s)</p>
<p>On inspection, you can apply the approach of 5s, that is:</p>
<p>a) Shape: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Note contour - is it round, oval, irregular or pendulous?</li>
<li>Longitudinal, ovoid in primigravida</li>
<li>Rround in multipara.</li>
<li>Broad in transverse lie.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Size: Should correspond with the supposed period of gestation</p>
<p>c) Skin: - The dark line of pigmentation which is linea nigra is seen any rash?</p>
<p>d) Striae gravidarum</p>
<p>e) Scar - Any operation scar(c/s)</p>
<p>Palpation:</p>
<p>On palpation, use the Leopoldâ€™s Maneuver. There are four steps in Leopoldâ€™s Maneuver</p>
<ol>
<li>Fundal height and fundal palpation (1st Leopold Maneuver). During this examine:</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Fundal Height</p>
<p>At about 12 to 14 weeks of pregnancy, the uterus is palpated above the symphysis pubis as a firm globular sphere; it reaches the umbilicus at 20 to 22 weeks, the xiphoidal process at 36 weeks, and then often returns to about 4 cm below the xiphoid due to â€œlighteningâ€ at 40 weeks.</p>
<p>Method: Measure distance of fundus with points on abdomen and assessing the fundal height in finger breadth below the xiphisternum or measure by centimeter.</p>
<p>b) Fundal Palpation</p>
<p>Purpose - To know lie and presentation.</p>
<p>Method: - Use 2 hands using palms of hands palpate on either side of the fundus. Fingers held close together, palpate the upper pole of then uterus and feel that as it is hard or soft or irregular.</p>
<p>34 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-2897da3f.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure: Fundal palpation</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Lateral Palpation: (2nd Leopled maneuver)</li>
</ol>
<p>Purpose-To know lie and position</p>
<p>Method: - always facing the mother, fix the hand on the center of the abdomen, fix the right hand and palpate with left hand and vice versa. Note the regularity; the regular side is the back</p>
<p>35 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-28f006c9.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure : Lateral palpation.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Deep pelvic Palpation: (3rd Leopoldel Maneuver)</li>
</ol>
<p>Purpose -To Know Presentation &amp; Attitude</p>
<p>Method: - Feel presenting part, is it hard or soft while</p>
<p>Palpating for the presenting part feel for eminences on back side.</p>
<p>36 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-b72d68ff.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg">
Figure : Deep pelvic palpation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-pawlick-s-grip-4th-leopard-maneuver">4. Pawlick's Grip: (4th Leopard Maneuver)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-pawlick-s-grip-4th-leopard-maneuver" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The lower pole of the uterus is grasped with the right hand the midwife facing the women's head, feel the occiput and sinciput, note which is lower.</p>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES -RUGENDO</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-aa7ffd79.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg">
Figure : Pwlick's grip.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="auscultation">Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On auscultation:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Check Fetal heart, rate and rhythm, count for one minute if regular.</li>
<li>Method: Use Pinards stethoscope. Hand should not touch it while listening. Ear must be in close from contact with stethoscope,</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember that during abdominal examination: -</p>
<ul>
<li>The client is asked to empty her bladder and then to lie on her back on a couch with the arms by her sides.</li>
<li>Inspect the abdomen for the shape, size, scars and foetal movements. Any abnormality detected is referred for further investigations.</li>
</ul>
<p>38 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Estimate the height of the fundus and compare it with the calculated EDD. This helps you to assess foetal growth and detect any deviations from the normal.</p>
<p>Check for varicosities at the back of the leg. Ask the woman to remove any tight clothing at the leg. At this time, it is also important to check for phlebitis by looking for any reddened areas.</p>
<p>Palpate the sides of the abdomen to locate the foetal back in order to determine the position. You do this by facing the patient and then supporting the uterus with your right hand. Keep pushing the foetus with your left hand towards the right. Reverse the order to feel the left side of the uterus.</p>
<p>Palpate the lower pole of the uterus, just above the pelvic brim.</p>
<p>Ask the mother to bend her knees slightly in order to relax the abdominal muscles and ask her to breath steadily with her mouth open.</p>
<p>Facing the foot of the bed, mark the brim of the pelvis with your hands and cup what presents between them. If the head is presenting, a smooth surface will be felt.</p>
<p>If you do not find the head in the pelvic brim or at the fundus, suspect a transverse lie. This will be significant only after the 36th week of gestation.</p>
<p>The foetal heart sounds are listened to last, so as to assess the foetal wellbeing. The Pinard's foetal stethoscope is commonly used to hear the foetal heart.</p>
<p>As you perform the physical examination, talk to the mother and check her facial reaction as you palpate the abdomen. When you complete the procedure reassure the mother.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="findings-of-abdominal-examinations">Findings of Abdominal Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#findings-of-abdominal-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All these are recorded upon completion of the exercise and they include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Gestational age, which is estimated as per the size of the fundus.- fundal height</li>
<li>Lie, which refers to the relationship between the long axis of the foetus and that of the mother and can either be longitudinal, transverse or oblique.</li>
<li>Attitude, which refers to the relationship of the foetal head and limbs to its trunk. It is most commonly flexion.</li>
<li>Presentation, which means the foetal part that is lying at the pelvic brim or in the lower pole of the uterus and can either be vertex, breach, face, shoulder or brow. The most common is the vertex. Note that vertex/brow/face all refer to head presentation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<ul>
<li>Denominator is the name given to the presenting part for example, occiput for vertex, sacrum for breech and mentum for face.</li>
<li>Position, which refers to the relationship between the denominator of the presentation and the landmarks of the pelvic brim.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other components of physical examination include:</p>
<p>a) Pelvic assessment
Can be achieved through:
By x-ray of the pelvis
Clinical (assessing sign of contracted pelvis)
Head fitting</p>
<p>b) Genito-Urinary System
Check on:
Frequency of micturition
For abnormal discharge</p>
<p>c) Circulatory System
Varicosities: - Varicose veins may occur in the legs, anus (hemorrhoids) and vulva.
Vulval varicosities are rare and very painful.</p>
<p>d) The Vulva
Check on:
Vulval warts
Purulent irritating discharge</p>
<p>e) The Lower Limbs
Examine for bones alignment and deformities.
Check pitting edema in the lower limbs by applying fingertip pressure for 10 seconds over the tibial bone.</p>
<p>Laboratory test
All pregnant women should do ANC Profile (Basic laboratory tests)
These tests include: -
Urinalysis (For Protein, glucose and ketones)
Hemoglobin levels
V.D.R.L.(for syphilis)
Rhesus factor
Blood group
Bs/Mps(Malaria test)
TB Screening.</p>
<p>Share health messages with the mother on:
The advantages of antenatal visits
Use of LLITNs
Drug compliance.
Use of tetanus toxoid vaccine.</p>
<p>40 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Rest and exercise</p>
<p>Clothing should be comfortable</p>
<p>Breast care.</p>
<p>Diet and nutrition - Rich in Iron and protein</p>
<p>Individualized birth plan.</p>
<p>Counsel for HIV</p>
<p>Educate the mother on danger signs during pregnancy.</p>
<p>Educate the mother on the following danger signs during pregnancy:</p>
<ul>
<li>Per Vaginal bleeding.</li>
<li>Convulsions/fits</li>
<li>Reduced fetal movements</li>
<li>Persistent Frontal or recurring headaches</li>

<li>Sudden swelling</li>
<li>Rupture of the membranes</li>
<li>Premature onset of contractions.</li>
<li>Foul smelling vaginal discharge</li>
<li>Blurred vision.</li>
<li>Excessive nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>Fever (38Â°C and above)</li>
</ul>
<p>Edema</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="elimination-of-mother-to-child-transmission-of-hiv-emtct">Elimination of Mother to Child Transmission of HIV(eMTCT).<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elimination-of-mother-to-child-transmission-of-hiv-emtct" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Overview and biology of HIV.</p>
<p>HIV (Human Immunodeficiency Virus) is a retrovirus in the family of Lentivirus.</p>
<p>Its genetic material consists of a single-stranded ribonucleic acid (RNA)</p>
<p>The viral particle is spherical in shape with a diameter of 80-100 nanometers (nm).</p>
<p>There are two types of HIV, namely:</p>
<p>a) HIV â€“ 1</p>
<ul>
<li>It is found worldwide</li>
<li>It is the main cause of the worldwide pandemic</li>
<li>HIV-1 has many subtypes: A-K</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>A-E are the predominant subtypes</p>
<p>A: -W. Africa, E. Africa, Central Africa East Europe &amp; Middle East
B: -N. America, Europe, Middle East, E. Asia, Latin America
C:- S. Africa, S. Asia, Ethiopia
D:- E. Africa
E:- S. E. Asia</p>
<p>b) HIV â€“ 2</p>
<p>It is mainly found in West Africa, Mozambique and Angola.
It causes a similar illness to HIV â€“ 1
It is less efficiently transmissible rarely causing vertical transmission
Less aggressive with slower disease progression</p>
<p>Structure Of Human Immunodeficiency Virus</p>
<p>Has an outer double lipid membrane, (derived from the host membrane).
The lipid membrane is lined by a matrix protein.
The lipid membrane is studded with the surface glycoprotein (gp) 120 and the transmembrane gp 41 protein.
These glycoprotein spikes surround the cone-shaped protein core.
HIV Glycoproteins: that is, gp120 and gp41 mediate the entry of virus into the host cells.
The core (capsid) is made up of several proteins with P24 being the main protein. Within the capsid are two identical single strands of RNA (the viral genetic material) and viral enzymes</p>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-a0a7a559.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<p>a) Most important: Reverse Transcriptase (RT), Protease and Integrase.
b) RT converts viral single-stranded RNA into a double stranded deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA). DNA is incorporated into host nucleus as the proviral DNA.
c) Integrase facilitates integration of the DNA into the host's chromosomal DNA.
d) Protease enzyme splits generated macro-proteins into smaller viral proteins (core, envelope &amp; regulatory proteins and enzymes) which go into forming new viral particles.</p>
<p>HIV life cycle</p>
<p>HIV life cycle has the following stages: -</p>
<p>a) Binding, Fusion and Entry
b) Transcription
c) Integration &amp; Replication
d) Budding
e) Maturation</p>
<p>Binding:</p>
<ul>
<li>Glycoprotein GP 120 binds to the host cell surface receptor (CD4 molecule) and coreceptor (CCR5/CXCR4) for successful entry.</li>
</ul>
<p>44 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<ul>
<li>Can also bind to CXCR2, CXCR3 and hitch ride on B-cells to lymph nodes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fusion-and-entry">Fusion and Entry:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fusion-and-entry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Viral binding to host cell triggers fusion of the viral and host cell membranes. This mediated by gp41</li>
<li>Allows entry of virus core into host cell cytoplasm</li>
<li>Core protein dissolved by host enzymes releasing viral RNA and enzymes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="transcription-integration">Transcription &amp; Integration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transcription-integration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reverse transcriptase converts the viral RNA into a single strand of DNA</li>
<li>RT also acts as a DNA polymerase to produce a partner strand of DNA to match the original template resulting in a double stranded DNA (dsDNA) but no proof-reading ability</li>
<li>The DNA enters the host cell nucleus</li>
<li>Integrase catalyses the process of integration of the viral DNA into the host cell's DNA to form provirus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="replication">Replication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#replication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Integrated viral DNA turns the host cell into a "factory" for manufacturing more virus.</p>
<p>Viral proteins are produced as a single multi-protein molecule. Viral proteins cleaved by protease enzyme</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="budding-and-maturation">Budding and Maturation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budding-and-maturation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Viral proteins together with RNA gather at the membrane of the CD4+ cells</li>
<li>Viral particles are formed which bud off the cell and enter the bloodstream</li>
</ul>
<p>The CD4 cells are often destroyed by HIV virus infection and replication resulting in profound immunodeficiency.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>46 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hiv-life-cycle-summary">HIV LIFE CYCLE: Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hiv-life-cycle-summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-cb04c9d3.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<p>Natural History of HIV Infection.</p>
<p>The natural history of HIV infection has the following stages: -</p>
<p>a) Primary infection (sero-conversion) - On exposure, there is a 2-4 week period of intense viral replication and widespread dissemination of virus characterized by</p>
<p>High plasma viral load (RNA)</p>
<p>Rapid decline in CD4 count</p>
<p>In some cases an acute illness occurs. Lasts from 1-2 weeks, but it is rarely diagnosed. Symptoms if present resemble those of other viral illnesses; requires high index of suspicion.</p>
<p>Symptom resolution with reduction in plasma viremia due to development of an immune response and antibodies to the virus</p>
<p>b) Asymptomatic Disease (Latency) stage.</p>
<p>Patients then enter a stage of asymptomatic disease phase lasting on average 2-10 years (clinical latency)</p>
<p>Characterized by gradual decline in CD4 count. Rate depends on viral load</p>
<p>c) Symptomatic stage.</p>
<p>Viral load continues to rise causing:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increased demands on immune system as production of CD4 cells cannot match destruction</li>
<li>Increased susceptibility to common infections (URTI, pneumonia, skin etc)</li>
</ul>
<p>d) Progression of HIV infection to AIDS.</p>
<p>This is Late-stage of HIV progression characterized by markedly reduction in CD4 count and the development of opportunistic infections, selected tumors, wasting, and neurological complications.</p>
<p>It signals progression of HIV infection to Acquired Immune deficiency syndrome.</p>
<p>WHO Clinical Staging of HIV infection.</p>
<p>World Health Organization(WHO) developed criteria for staging HIV infection as follows: -</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Clinical Stage</th><th>Selected Symptoms</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Primary HIV Infection</td><td>1. Unrecognized Acute retroviral syndrome</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ol start="2">
<li>Acute febrile illness 2-4 wks post-exposure often with lymphadenopathy and skin manifestations  |
|  Stage I | 1. Asymptomatic</li>
<li>Persistent generalized lymphadenopathy  |
|  Stage II | 1. Moderate unexplained weight loss (&lt;10% of presumed or measured body weight)  |
|  Stage III | 2. Recurrent upper respiratory tract infections (sinusitis, bronchitis, otitis media, pharyngitis)</li>
<li>Herpes zoster (past or current episodes in last 2 years)</li>
<li>Angular cheilitis</li>
<li>Recurrent oral ulcerations (2 or more episodes in 6 months)</li>
<li>Papular pruritic eruptions; Seborrhoeic dermatitis; Fungal nail infections of fingers</li>
</ol>
<p>Conditions where a presumptive diagnosis can be made using clinical signs or simple investigations</p>
<ul>
<li>Severe weight loss (&gt;10% presumed or measured body weight)</li>
<li>Unexplained chronic diarrhea for &gt; 1 month  |</li>
</ul>
<p>47 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>48 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>|  Stage IV | Conditions where a presumptive diagnosis can be made using clinical signs or simple investigations:</p>
<p>HIV wasting syndrome
Pneumocystis carinii pneumonia (PCP)
Recurrent severe bacterial pneumonia
Cryptococcal meningitis
Toxoplasmosis of the brain
Chronic orolabial, genital or anorectal herpes simplex infection for &gt; 1 month
Kaposiâ€™s sarcoma (KS)
HIV encephalopathy
Extrapulmonary tuberculosis
Cryptosporidiosis, with diarrhea &gt;1 month
Isosporiasis
Conditions where confirmatory diagnostic testing is necessary</p>
<p>Candidiasis of the esophagus or airways
Cytomegalovirus (CMV) retinitis or disease of organs (other than liver, spleen, or lymph nodes)
Non-typhoid salmonella septicemia (NTS)
Lymphoma cerebral or B cell NHL
Invasive cervical carcinoma
Visceral Leishmaniasis
Cryptococcosis (extrapulmonary)
Disseminated non tuberculous mycobacterial infection
Progressive multifocal leukoencephalopathy
Any disseminated endemic mycosis (e.g. histoplasmosis)  |
| --- | --- |</p>
<p>HIV testing.</p>
<p>The importance of HIV testing includes: -</p>
<p>a) Diagnosis of HIV.
b) To enable Staging of HIV disease (especially through CD4 T cell analysis)
c) To determine the prognosis of HIV infection (mainly through CD4 T cell analysis and viral load)
d) To determine when to initiate preventive therapies and ART(CD4 T cell analysis)
e) To assess response to ART (CD4 T cell analysis/viral load)
f) To evaluate patients for toxicity to ARVs (RFT/LFT)</p>
<p>Approaches in HIV testing.</p>
<p>The following approaches are applied in HIV Testing.</p>
<ol>
<li>Voluntary counseling and testing</li>
<li>Diagnostic HIV testing</li>
<li>Provider initiated counseling and testing</li>
<li>Mandatory HIV testing and screening</li>
</ol>
<p>Types of HIV tests.</p>
<p>Types of HIV tests are classified into two, namely:</p>
<p>a) Antibody based test.</p>
<p>i. Enzyme Immunosorbent Assay (ELISA)
ii. Western Blot
iii. Rapid Tests</p>
<p>b) Viral detection methods/ antigen based tests</p>
<p>i. PCR</p>
<p>For the purpose of this lesson, we will discuss Rapid test in diagnosing HIV. The learner should read further on other types of HIV tests.</p>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES -RUGENDO</p>
<p>Rapid HIV tests. (RDTs)</p>
<p>They were developed in the late 1980s</p>
<p>They can be performed in less than 20 minutes</p>
<p>It can be performed easily without sophisticated instruments.</p>
<p>Results are available immediately.</p>
<p>Examples â€“ Determine, First response and Oraquick.</p>
<p>The learner should note that HIV testing approaches is highly dynamic hence one should keep updated from time to time.</p>
<p>Oraquick is designed for self-testing.</p>
<p>Elimination of Mother to Child Transmission of HIV(eMTCT).</p>
<p>eMTCT can be defined as measures and interventions put in place to avert transmission of HIV from the mother to the baby.</p>
<p>It was formerly referred as PMTCT (Prevention of Mother to Child Transmission of HIV), However it changed to eMTCT that endeavours to achieve zero transmission of HIV to babies.</p>
<p>Mother to Child Transmission occurs when the HIV virus is passed from the mother to the baby. This happens as follows.</p>
<p>During pregnancy 5-10%</p>
<p>During labour and delivery 10-20%</p>
<p>During breastfeeding 5-20%</p>
<p>BENEFITS OF Emtct</p>
<p>Benefits of eMTCT includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Improved child health and child survival</li>
<li>Decreased burden to the health care system</li>
<li>Increased public understanding of the HIV/AIDS epidemic</li>
<li>Help increase acceptance of people living with HIV/AIDS</li>
</ul>
<p>FOUR PILLARS OF W.H.O TO REDUCE MTCT</p>
<ol>
<li>Preventing of unintended pregnancy in HIV+ women through family planning.</li>
<li>Prevention of HIV infection in women through use of ABCD</li>
<li>eMTCT in pregnancy: testing and counselling to identify HIV+ women; provide ARVS to mother and baby; use of infection prevention practices.</li>
<li>Care and support to those living with HIV/AIDS.</li>
</ol>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Four Pronged approach to eMTCT.</p>
<p>The four prongs of eMTCT are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Primary prevention of HIV infection in women.</li>
<li>Prevention of unintended pregnancies among HIV-infected women.</li>
<li>Interventions to reduce transmission from HIV infected and lactating women to their children.</li>
<li>Care and support of women, children and families infected and affected by HIV and AIDS(eMTCT-Plus).</li>
</ol>
<p>Effects of pregnancy on HIV-AIDS</p>
<p>Effects of pregnancy on HIV-AIDS includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Immune response is suppressed</li>
<li>CD4 counts decline more rapidly compared to non-pregnant women</li>
<li>At increased risk of UTI</li>
<li>It may accelerate the progress to full blown AIDS or quicker deterioration if the final stage of AIDS.</li>
</ul>
<p>Effects of HIV-AIDS on the pregnancy</p>
<p>Effects of HIV/AIDS on the pregnancy includes: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Associated with other STIs</li>
<li>They are more likely to have candidal vaginitis</li>
<li>Increase of other infections e.g UTIs</li>
<li>Rate of ectopic pregnancy is 4 times higher in HIV +ve women.</li>
<li>Higher rates of abortions and stillbirths have been reported in some African studies</li>
<li>Preterm labour and PPROM</li>
<li>Higher rate of abruptio placenta in HIV +ve women.</li>
<li>Chorio-amniotis is more common in women with HIV infection.</li>
<li>HIV is a major cause of anaemia in pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>Risk factor for Mother To Child Transmission OF HIV.</p>
<p>Risk factor for Mother To Child Transmission OF HIV can be classified as:-</p>
<p>51 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>a) Viral factor</p>
<p>Clinical stage of infection: new and advanced infections</p>
<p>High viral load in blood and genital tract</p>
<p>b) Maternal factors</p>
<p>Low maternal CD4 count (the number of cells per cubic millimetre of blood)</p>
<p>Vitamin A Deficiency</p>
<p>Unprotected sex with multiple and infected partners</p>
<p>STIs and other co infections</p>
<p>Mother not taking ARV agents</p>
<p>Malaria infection in pregnant women.</p>
<p>Breast infections or disorders.</p>
<p>c) Obstetric and gynaecological factors</p>
<p>Invasive foetal monitoring procedures</p>
<p>Duration of membrane rupture</p>
<p>Routine episiotomy</p>
<p>Placental disruption</p>
<p>Vaginal delivery</p>
<p>Prolonged labour.</p>
<p>d) Infant factors</p>
<p>Breastfeeding (longer duration of breastfeeding)</p>
<p>Preterm delivery</p>
<p>Neonatal birth injuries</p>
<p>Vigorous naso-gastric tube suction</p>
<p>Infections eg oral ulcers or thrush.</p>
<p>HIV Testing and Counselling in eMTCT.</p>
<p>Definition of terms.</p>
<p>a) HIV testing: process of determining if client is infected with HIV</p>
<p>b) HIV counselling: confidential dialogue between an individual or a couple and a healthcare worker (HCW) to help clients examine their risk of acquiring or transmitting HIV. HIV counselling should be tailored to the risk behaviour, circumstances and special needs of the client</p>
<p>HIV Testing and Counselling in eMTCT provides: -</p>
<p>Information about HIV status</p>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Opportunity to identify women with HIV and empower them to make decisions to prevent MTCT</p>
<p>Opportunity to identify women who are HIV negative and empower them to remain negative</p>
<p>HIV testing and counselling should be anchored on the following three principles:</p>
<ol>
<li>Confidentiality</li>
<li>Informed consent</li>
<li>Post-test support and services</li>
</ol>
<p>Main approaches applied in HIV testing and Counselling in eMTCT.</p>
<p>There are two main approaches utilized in eMTCT, they are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Provider-initiated</li>
<li>Client-initiated</li>
</ol>
<p>Both approaches include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Basic information about providing HIV testing</li>
<li>Risks and benefits of testing</li>
</ul>
<p>Steps in HIV Testing and Counselling.</p>
<p>There are three key stages in HIV Testing and Counselling as described below.</p>
<p>a) Pre-test Information and Counselling.</p>
<p>The purpose of the pre-test session in eMTCT settings is to provide the woman or couple with adequate information to make an informed decision about HIV testing.</p>
<p>Pre-test session models can be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Group counselling.</li>
<li>Individual counselling</li>
<li>Couple counselling</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Testing.</p>
<ul>
<li>Testing of HIV in eMTCT is commonly done using Rapid Diagnostic Tests (Rapid test).</li>
<li>Rapid HIV tests detect antibodies associated with HIV in whole blood or saliva.</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Blood is the most common used specimen in HIV testing</p>
<p>Rapid HIV tests</p>
<ul>
<li>Accurate results within 20-40 minutes</li>
<li>Can be done in the clinic setting</li>
<li>Accurate when performed correctly</li>
<li>Usually performed on serum or whole blood (by fingerprick or venous sample); some rapid HIV tests use saliva eg oraquick.</li>
<li>HCWs can be trained to perform the tests</li>
<li>Usually do not require special equipment, electricity or refrigeration</li>
</ul>
<p>Benefits of rapid HIV testing include:</p>
<ul>
<li>On-site testing and same day results</li>
<li>Lower risk of administrative error</li>
<li>Accepted by clients</li>
<li>Fewer resources required: Human resources, Resources at the facility, Financial resources</li>
<li>Lower risk of occupational exposure</li>
</ul>
<p>Interpreting results.</p>
<ul>
<li>The care provider should educate and explain to the client on how to interpret results.</li>
<li>The client should understand that:</li>
<li>A positive HIV test means that antibodies to HIV are present. It does not mean that the client has AIDS</li>
<li>A negative HIV test can mean: The person is not infected with HIV, or The person is infected with the virus but is in the window period</li>
</ul>
<p>Steps in HIV Testing can be summarized as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>A specimen is obtained</li>
<li>The specimen is processed</li>
<li>Test is conducted by a HCW or laboratory technician</li>
<li>The client is told their result</li>
<li>HCW provides post-test counselling, support and appropriate referrals</li>
</ol>
<p>When performing HIV testing, you are required to observe the following points: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Infection control and Standard Precautions</li>
<li>Proper labelling</li>
<li>Proper specimen collection procedures</li>
</ul>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Required volume per test</p>
<p>Proper reagents per test</p>
<p>Correct timing per test</p>
<p>Interpretation of results</p>
<p>Proper record-keeping</p>
<p>Proper disposal procedures</p>
<p>Factors that can affect test results.</p>
<p>Storage and handling of test kits</p>
<p>Changes in the environment</p>
<p>Accuracy of equipment (external and internal controls)</p>
<p>Shelf-life of the chemicals for the tests (reagents)</p>
<p>Technique for sample collection</p>
<p>Quality of sample</p>
<p>Use of equipment</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-f9b3a92e.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<p>55 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>c) Post-test Counselling.</p>
<p>All HIV test results, whether positive or negative, must be given in person, privately (as a single client or couple)</p>
<p>Put the client or couple at ease</p>
<p>Remember that client can either turn negative or positive.</p>
<p>When Client Tests HIV-negative</p>
<ul>
<li>Provide HIV test result and assess understanding of result</li>
<li>Identify and address client questions</li>
</ul>
<p>Discuss:</p>
<ul>
<li>Partner HIV testing and disclosure</li>
<li>Safer sex and risk reduction</li>
<li>Exclusive breastfeeding</li>
<li>Antenatal care, post-delivery care</li>
<li>Importance of delivering in a healthcare facility</li>
<li>Infant care</li>
</ul>
<p>Provide referrals, take-home information</p>
<p>When Client Tests HIV-positive</p>
<ul>
<li>Client reactions to results can range from acceptance to disbelief</li>
<li>Remain non-judgemental, supportive and confident throughout the counselling process</li>
<li>Provide all key eMTCT messages during the initial post-test counselling session</li>
<li>Encourage client to return for her ANC visits and follow-up HIV post-test counselling</li>
</ul>
<p>Discuss:</p>
<ul>
<li>ARV therapy or prophylaxis</li>
<li>Infant feeding options</li>
<li>Treatment and support services for client and family</li>
</ul>
<p>Disclosure of HIV Status. Clients who disclose are in a better position to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Encourage partner(s) to be tested</li>
<li>Prevent transmission of HIV to partner(s)</li>
<li>Access PMTCT interventions</li>
</ul>
<p>56 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<ul>
<li>Receive support from partner(s) and family</li>
</ul>
<p>Management of HIV positive clients during pregnancy.</p>
<p>As discussed earlier during FANC, the midwife should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Provide Primary prevention services during pregnancy such as, Education about safer sex with use of condoms for mother and father, Early treatment of STIs, Safer sex during pregnancy and lactation</li>
<li>Ensure VCT services are offered to all pregnant women.</li>
<li>Understand that Antenatal visits are vital opportunities for eMTCT for both HIV-positive and HIV-negative women.</li>
<li>Every pregnant woman should be offered HIV testing.</li>
<li>HIV testing should be voluntary.</li>
<li>eMTCT depends on being able to identify women who can benefit from interventions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Care of HIV Positive women in FANC</p>
<p>Initial assessment should be conducted on HIV positive pregnant women, and should include:</p>
<p>Duration of known HIV+ status</p>
<p>Past history of HIV-related illness and HAART</p>
<p>WHO Staging</p>
<p>Status of other children, partner, and partner disclosure and referral</p>
<p>Any medications taken for HIV-related illness since beginning of pregnancy</p>
<p>Women with HIV should have medical care during pregnancy</p>
<p>Look for and treat other infections such as malaria, anemia etc</p>
<p>Nutritional counselling and supplements</p>
<p>Monitor the HIV infection</p>
<p>Counselling about infant feeding, other infections, danger signs etc</p>
<p>Counsel the mother on birth preparedness.</p>
<p>Early detection of opportunistic infections.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Provide prophylactic(preventive) intervention such IFAS, Tetanus Toxoid, use of LLITNs, cotrimoxazole(Septrin) prophylaxis.</p>
<p>Antiretroviral treatment.</p>
<ul>
<li>All pregnant women irrespective of CD4 Count or Viral load should be initiated on HAART immediately.</li>
<li>HAART (Highly Active Antiretroviral Therapy) is a treatment regimen comprising of a combination of three or more antiretroviral drugs. This co-administration of different drugs helps in suppressing viral replication through several mechanisms.</li>
<li>The current HAART regimen used in Kenya is a combination of tdf(tenofovir)+3tc(Lamivudine)+efv (efavirenz).</li>
<li>All HIV positive pregnant women should be started on Cotrimoxazole (Septrin) prophylaxis to protect the mother from bacterial opportunistic infections.</li>
</ul>
<p>Management during labour</p>
<p>Management during labour and delivery should include:</p>
<p>Antiretroviral therapy</p>
<p>The mother should continue with HAART and ctx as prescribed.</p>
<p>The following procedures should be avoided in order to prevent injury to the foetus.</p>
<ul>
<li>Artificial rupture of membranes</li>
<li>Scalp electrodes</li>
<li>Amnioinfusion</li>
<li>Amniocentesis</li>
<li>Forceps and vacuum delivery</li>
<li>Oropharngeal suctioning of the new-born to prevent injury to the mucosa</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevention of contamination with maternal blood and fluids</p>
<ul>
<li>Perineal trauma and episiotomies should be avoided</li>
<li>Baby should be wiped immediately after birth.</li>
<li>Perform immediate clamping and cutting of the cord.</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevention of intrauterine contamination with vaginal secretion</p>
<ul>
<li>Shorten length of ruptured membranes to less than 4 hours</li>
<li>Limit the number of vagina examination (Avoid too many unnecessary Vaginal examinations).</li>
</ul>
<p>58 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Prevent and treat other infections and complications.
Check for and manage UTIs at the start of labour</p>
<p>Monitor labour carefully using partograph.
Using a partograph will enable the midwife to detect any complication during labour.</p>
<p>Caesarean section
Evaluate and consider Caesarean Section. Available evidence shows that Caesarean Section reduces incidence of HIV transmission to the baby.</p>
<p>Management during postpartum</p>
<ul>
<li>During post-natal period, the care now focusses both to the mother and the baby.</li>
<li>In addition to immediate maternal care after delivery, the mother should: -</li>
<li>Continue and Adhere to HAART and ctx</li>
<li>Advised and counsel of appropriate contraception and child spacing.</li>
<li>Advised on feeding options:</li>
<li>Exclusive breastfeeding reduces the chance of HIV transmission to the baby. Breastfeeding should be exclusive for 6 months, if breastfeeding is chosen teach the mother good breastfeeding technique to avoid cracked nipples and mastitis which can increase MTCT. Mixed feeding, presence of mastitis and cracked nipples increases the risk of HIV transmission.</li>
<li>Formula feeding. AFASS criteria to see if mother is able to follow exclusive formula feeding (EFF) is used:</li>
<li>Acceptability: is EFF acceptable for the mother</li>
<li>Feasibility: is the mother able to begin EFF correctly for the required period</li>
<li>Affordability: is the mother able to afford the cost of EFF</li>
<li>Sustainability: will the mother be able to continue the recommended EFF standards for the required period</li>
<li>Safety: will the mother be able to practice EFF safely</li>
<li>In addition to essential new-born care, care of HIV-Exposed Infant (HEI) should also include:-</li>
<li>Initiation of Nevirapine at birth up to 12 weeks as per the babyâ€™s weight.</li>
<li>Nevirapine should be issued to the HIV positive mother at the first point of contact for the baby in case she delivers before reaching the hospital.</li>
</ul>
<p>59 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<ul>
<li>Nevirapine therapy to the baby should be started at birth or at the first contact with the exposed infant.</li>
<li>Infant prophylaxis with Nevirapine syrup should up to 12 weeks from birth for mothers on HAART</li>
<li>Infant prophylaxis with Nevirapine syrup should up to one week after cessation of breast feeding for mothers not on HAART.</li>
</ul>
<p>Initiation of Zidovudine (Syrup) at birth up to six weeks.</p>
<p>After 12 weeks Nevirapine is stopped.</p>
<p>The baby is put on Cotrimoxazole (Septrin) syrup from 6 weeks up to 18 months.</p>
<p>Infant PCR testing (Using Dry Blood Spots technique) is done at 6 weeks after birth, then 6 months after birth, the third is done at one year after birth and fourth and the last is done at 18 months after birth.</p>
<p>PCR result at 18 months is considered final.</p>
<p>Immunization schedule of HIV Exposed Infant (HEI) is similar to the national immunization schedule, however these infants receives a booster measles vaccine at 6 months in their life.</p>
<p>60 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Diagram showing a flow chart on infant HIV testing protocol</p>

<p>Mothers who were not tested for HIV during antenatal period can be counselled and tested during labour and postpartum period.</p>
<p>In the event the baby turns negative at 18 months, the mother and the baby maybe discharged from eMTCT program and continue with Comprehensive care services (CCC).</p>
