<p>63 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="normal-labour">Normal labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#normal-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Learning objectives</p>
<p>By the end of the unit, the learner should be able:</p>
<p>a) To Define normal labour
b) to differentiate between true and false labour.
c) To discuss management of a mother in labour.
d) To Explain the physiology of the onset of labour
e) To describe mechanisms of labour
f) To describe the stages of labour
g) To describe the physiological changes that occur during labour
h) To describe the management of normal labour and use of partograph</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition of labour.</p>
<p>Labour is a physiological process, characterized by rhythmic regular uterine contractions increasing in frequency and intensity, accompanied by progressive cervical effacement and dilatation, and descent of the presenting part.</p>
<p>Labour may be spontaneous or induced</p>
<p>Definition of normal labour.</p>
<p>Physiological process, which commences spontaneously at term (37 completed weeks) with rhythmic regular uterine contractions of increasing intensity and frequency, accompanied by progressive cervical effacement and dilatation, and descent of the presenting part (preferably cephalic/Vertex), resulting in expulsion of a healthy foetus, a complete placenta and membranes and a healthy mother.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-normal-labour">Characteristics of normal labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-normal-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) It is spontaneous
b) It occurs at term(38-40 weeks) with regular uterine contractions
c) Completed within 18 hours
d) The presentation is vertex</p>
<p>e) No complications to the mother and the baby
f) Newborn requires minimal or no resuscitation.
g) expulsion of a healthy single foetus, a complete placenta and membranes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-onset-of-labour">Causes of onset of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-onset-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Associated factors include:
a) Hormonal factors: fetal cortisol, prostaglandin, oxytocin, estrogen and relaxin</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Oxytocin increases</li>
<li>Progesterone decrease</li>
<li>Oestrogen increases</li>
<li>Prostanglandins increases</li>
<li>Relaxin increases</li>
<li>Fetal cortisol increases
b) Mechanical stimulation:</li>
<li>Foetal engagement</li>
<li>Overstretching of uterus</li>
<li>Rupture of membranes</li>
<li>General fluid pressure</li>
<li>Fetal axis pressure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanisms-of-labour">Mechanisms of labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are series of movements the foetus maneuvers during delivery. These mechanisms of labour are:-
a) Engagement and Descent
b) Flexion
c) Internal rotation of head
d) Extension of the head
e) Restitution
f) Internal rotation of shoulders/ External rotation of the head
g) Lateral flexion</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>h) Expulsion</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="engagement">Engagement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#engagement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It occurs when the fetal presenting passes through the pelvic inlet/pelvic brim</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="descent">Descent<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#descent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is the progressive downward movement of fetal presenting part through the pelvic cavity. Descent is aided by uterine contractions and ambulation. The progressive movement of the fetal head into the pelvis</p>
<p>The fetal head is divided into 5 parts</p>
<p>a) When the whole head is above the brim, descent is 5/5â€”the sinciput and occiput above the brim
b) 4/5 sinciput prominent and occiput descending
c) 3/5 sinciput rising, occiput can be tipped per vagina
d) 2/5 sinciput not so prominent
e) 1/5 sinciput and occiput not felt
f) 0/5 Head on pelvic floor</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>5/5</th><th>4/5</th><th>3/5</th><th>2/5</th><th>1/5</th><th>0/5</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Pelvic brim</td><td></td><td>Pelvic Cavity</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Completely above</td><td>Sinciput High Occiput Easily felt</td><td>Sinciput Easily felt Occiput Felt</td><td>Sinciput Felt Occiput Just felt</td><td>Sinciput Felt Occiput Not felt</td><td>None of head palpable</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="flexion">Flexion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#flexion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the fetal head touches the bony pelvis, there is flexion of the fetal head.</p>
<p>This helps in ensuring that the head engages in sub-occipital bregmatic (SOB) diameter.</p>
<p>65 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-rotation-of-the-head">Internal rotation of the head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>After flexion, the head rotate <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>8</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1/8</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1/8</span></span></span></span></span>th of a circle and the occiput presents in anterior position. This is aided by uterine contractions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="crowning">Crowning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#crowning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs when the nape of the neck has passed the pelvic outlet and its firmly held against the pubic arch and it does not recede even after cessation of contractions.</p>
<p>The parietal eminences pass through the bony outlet. At this stage the head no longer recedes between contractions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="extension-of-the-head">Extension of the head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extension-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Once the occiput has escaped from under the symphysis pubis, the head extends forward. Further extension allows the sinciput, face and chin to escape the perineum and the head is born by extension.</p>
<p>Extension is the result of action from two forces.</p>
<p>a) The abdominal and thoracic muscles exert downward pressure.
b) The pelvic floor and perineum resist this pressure and push the head forward and upward through the weak area, which is the vagina.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="restitution">Restitution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restitution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The head turns <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>8</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1/8</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1/8</span></span></span></span></span> of the circle to the left, back to where it was before. This takes place to undo the twist, which occurred during the previous internal rotation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-rotation-of-the-shoulders">Internal rotation of the shoulders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-shoulders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When the head is passing through the level of the ischial spines and the outlet in anterior posterior position, the shoulders enters in the oblique diameter of the pelvis.</p>
<p>As the restitution is taking place, the shoulders which were in oblique diameter to the pelvis, rotate forward 1/8 of a circle and now engages in the anterior posterior diameter of the outlet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lateral-flexion">Lateral flexion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lateral-flexion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Following these movements, the body bends sideways to follow the curve of the birth canal.</p>
<p>The anterior shoulder escapes under the symphysis pubis and the posterior shoulder sweeps the perineum.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>The body of the baby is born by lateral flexion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="expulsion">Expulsion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expulsion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The effects of uterine contractions enable expulsion of the other parts of the baby's body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-common-to-all-mechanisms-of-labour">Principles common to all mechanisms of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-common-to-all-mechanisms-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are three principles common to all mechanisms of labour which are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Descent takes place</li>
<li>Whichever part leads and first meets the resistance of the pelvic floor will rotate forward until it comes under the symphysis pubis</li>
<li>Whatever that emerges from the pelvis will pivot around the pubic bone.</li>
</ol>
<p>Admitting a mother in labour ward.</p>
<p>Admitting a mother in labour ward is an integral part in management of labour. Purpose of admitting a mother into labour ward includes: -</p>
<p>a) To ensure the safety of the mother and fetus during labour
b) To plan accurately for the course of labour and birth
c) To promote a rewarding experience for the entire birthing family.</p>
<p>As a midwife you should ensure the following activities are carried out during admission, namely:-</p>
<p>Greet and create a rapport with the mother.</p>
<p>Ask for ANC card/booklet from the mother</p>
<p>Information that can be obtained from ANC Card/booklet include: -</p>
<p>a) Number of ANC attendance
b) Findings of previous physical examination
c) ANC profile (blood group and Rhesus factor, etc)
d) LMP and Expected date of delivery
e) Services provided during ANC visits
f) Any special care required.
g) Treatment of any infection or condition during pregnancy</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>h) Risk factors identified during ANC clinic</p>
<p>History taking (Biodata, chief complaints, history of presenting illness, past obstetric history, current obstetric history, past medical-surgical history, gynecological history, socio-economic history, family history and family planning history.</p>
<p>History of current pregnancy should focus on:-</p>
<p>a) LMP and EDD
b) Presence of show
c) Presence or absence of uterine contractions
d) Onset of the uterine contractions
e) Characteristics of the contractions
f) Rupture of membranes
g) Food and drugs taken for the last four hours</p>
<p>In past obstetric history you can use the format shown below</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Pregnancy and number of ANC attendants</th><th>Pregnancy and number of ANC attendants</th><th>Outcome</th><th>Puerperium</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Take observations and measurements:</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>a) Temperature, pulse, blood pressure
b) Weight and height</p>
<p>Thorough physical examination: General physical examination, breast examination, abdominal, pelvic examination, vaginal examination.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Request for laboratory investigations-If the mother was attending ANC clinic you can obtain some form the records. If she has not been attending ANC clinic request for all the tests. Urinalysis should be done to all mothers in labour.</p>
<p>Inform the mother about the findings, Record and interpret the findings.</p>
<p>Findings of abdominal examination may include: -</p>
<p>a) Size and shape of the abdomen
b) Contours and scars
c) Skin colour and marks eg linea nigra, striae gravidurum.
d) Foetal movement
e) Fundal height
f) Presentation
g) Lie
h) Contractions
i) Foetal heart rate</p>
<p>Indication of a V.E in labour include:-</p>
<p>a) To check cervical effacement and dilatation
b) To check the presenting part
c) To check the state of the membranes
d) To rule out cord prolapse and cord presentation
e) To check moulding
f) To assess the liquor amni
g) To assess engagement
h) To assess for station
i) To determine the position
j) To assess progress of labour.</p>
<p>Key assessment during general physical examinations may include: -</p>
<p>a) Assessing for anemia
b) Assessing for oedema
c) Assessing for lymphadenopathy
d) Assessing for any swelling and scars</p>
<p>After performing all this you need to establish whether the mother is in labour and which stage of labour.</p>
<p>Admit the mother in first stage room</p>
<p>Management will depend with the stage of labour. (Now we will discuss labour according to stages of labour)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-p-s-that-influence-the-outcome-of-labour">4" P" s that influence the outcome of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-p-s-that-influence-the-outcome-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Power-Refers to the characteristics of uterine contractions
b) Passage-Refers to the size, shape and resistance of birth canal including bony pelvis, cervix, vagina and pelvic floor.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>c) Passenger- This refers to the size, lie and presentation of the fetus, as well as the placenta and membranes
d) Psyche- This refers to the emotional preparedness of the mother. The mother's perception of the process of birth is influenced by her self-confidence, her patterns of coping with uncertainty and stress, her own attitude and expectation about labour. Adrenaline released during fear reduces oxytocin production thus prolonging labour</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="true-versus-false-labour">True versus false labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#true-versus-false-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Differences between True and False labour are:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Features</th><th>True labour</th><th>False labour</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Contraction</td><td>Regular</td><td>Irregular</td></tr><tr><td>Interval between pains</td><td>Gradually shorten</td><td>Remain long</td></tr><tr><td>Intensity</td><td>Increases</td><td>Remain the same</td></tr><tr><td>Cervical dilation /effacement</td><td>Present and progressive</td><td>Absent</td></tr><tr><td>Bulging membranes</td><td>Present</td><td>Absent</td></tr><tr><td>Sedation and analgesics</td><td>Pain not stopped</td><td>Pain relieved</td></tr><tr><td>Descent of presenting part</td><td>Present and progressive</td><td>Absent</td></tr><tr><td>Location of pain</td><td>Lower abdomen and radiate to the back</td><td>Remains at lower abdomen</td></tr><tr><td>Premonitory signs of labour</td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>These are changes that occurs 2-3 weeks prior to the onset of labour.</p>
<p>They include: -</p>
<p>a) Lightening</p>
<p>70 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>b) Frequency of Micturition
c) Taking up of the cervix
d) Braxton Hicks contractions
e) Increased vaginal secretions
f) sudden rush of energy: due to change in levels of estrogen and progesterone
g) Increased backache and sacroiliac pressure
h) Bloody show</p>
<p>Pain during labour occurs as a result of:-
a) Hypoxia of the contracted myometrium
b) Compression of the nerve ganglia in the cervix and lower uterus
c) Stretching of the cervix during dilatation
d) Stretching of the peritoneum underlying the fundus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-stage-of-labour">FIRST STAGE OF LABOUR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>First stage is divided into two phases, namely: -
a) Latent- 0-4 cm dilatation.
b) Active-Begins from 4 cm to full cervical dilatation.</p>
<p>Length varies depending on parity, birth interval, psychological state, presentation, position, pelvic shape and size, characteristics of uterine contractions.</p>
<p>The duration of first stage of labor determines the duration of labor because it takes the most time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiology-of-first-stage-of-labour">Physiology of first Stage of labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiology-of-first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Physiological changes that takes place during first stage of labour includes: -
a) Fundal dominance-contraction starts and stays longer at fundus. Contractions begins at the fundus and spread downwards lasting at the fundus where it is most intense but the peak is reached simultaneously over the whole uterus and fades from all parts together. This permits cervical dilatation and allows strongly contracting fundus to expel the fetus.
b) Polarity-neuromuscular harmony between the segments. The term used to describe the neuromuscular harmony that exist between the upper and lower uterine segments. The upper uterine segment contracts strongly and retracts to expel the fetus while lower segment contracts slightly and dilates to allow expulsion of the fetus.</p>
<p>71 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>c) Contraction and retraction (shortening). The uterus contracts and retracts in labor. The contractions do not fade completely but muscle fibers retain some of the shortening of contraction and therefore do not relax completely. Retraction occurs when uterine muscles do not get back to their position after a contraction leading to effacement and cervical dilatation. During contractions, the upper segment becomes thicker and shorter; the cavity diminishes gradually while the lower segment becomes thinner. Uterine contractions usually increase in intensity, duration and frequency of contractions.</p>
<p>d) Formation of upper and lower uterine segment (Upper uterine segment becomes thicker and Lower uterine segment becomes thinner). A physiological Retraction ring/ridge is formed between the two segments. When this ring becomes pathological and visible during labour it is called bandl's ring.</p>
<p>e) Cervical effacement and dilation-taking up of cervix and enlargement of uterine os. Cervical dilatation is brought about by the upward traction exerted by the retracted muscle fibers of the upper segment. It is also aided by the pressure from a well-fitting presenting part.</p>
<p>f) Show-blood stained mucoid discharge. This is the blood stained mucous discharge that is seen within few hours after the labor starts. This is the mucous that was forming the cervical plug. The blood is from the ruptured capillaries as the chorion detaches from the decidua and effects of descending foetal presenting part.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-first-stage-of-labour">Management of First stage of labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Provide woman-centered individualized care.</p>
<p>b) Preform Abdominal examination (Review previous lesson on the indication of abdominal examination in labour).</p>
<p>c) Vaginal examination (Review previous lesson on the indication of vaginal examination during labour).</p>
<p>d) Determine if the mother is in true labour</p>
<p>e) Assess progress of labour.</p>
<p>f) Remember to:</p>
<p>i. Palpate uterine contractions
ii. Assessment of the cervix dilatation
iii. Determine effacement of the cervix: thinning of the cervix (%)
iv. Assess Consistency of the cervix: soft vs. hard. During labor the cervix becomes soft.
v. Determine Position of the cervix: posterior vs. anterior. During labor the cervix changes from posterior to anterior.
vi. Check if Membrane is intact or ruptured: assessed by fluid collection in the vagina</p>
<p>g) Encourage the woman to:</p>
<p>i. Empty her bladder regularly and do urinalysis 2hrly (Encourage the woman to empty her bladder every 1-2 hours, If the woman is not able to visit the toilet, offer privacy and</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>provide with a bed pan, A catheter is passed if the woman is unable to empty the bladder completely.</p>
<p>ii. Freely move about if membranes un ruptured to facilitate descent
iii. Encourage the mother to lie of left-lateral position
iv. Maintain oral intake of fluids and food as required
v. Provide emotional support
vi. Exercise breathing techniques
vii. Observe personal hygiene
viii. Have a chosen companion with her.</p>
<p>h) Monitor the following: -</p>
<p>i. Foetal movements â€“ FHR half hourly, membranes â€“ clear/meconium liquor
ii. Maternal conditions â€“ pulse Â½ hourly, BP 4 hrly, resp 4 hrly, temperature 2 hrly
iii. Progress of labour â€“ contractions, intensity, regular, frequency, duration; descent
iv. Lab findings â€“ urinalysis proteins, sugars Investigations, Hematology (Hematocrit, Hemoglobin, Blood Group, Rh, cross-match) Urine analysis, Protein (Albumin), Sugar, Ketone) Enhance good communication and support</p>
<p>i) Maintain vulva hygiene
j) Educate the mother on the expectations of second stage
k) Practice universal infection prevention and control protocols:-</p>
<p>i. Admit the woman in a clean environment.
ii. Control the no number of visitors in a birthing unit.
iii. Clean beds and rooms thoroughly after use.
iv. Encourage the woman to bathe and wash as she wishes.
v. Wash your hands before and after attending the client.
vi. Wear gloves when handling used sanitary pads, blood stained linen or body fluid.
vii. Invasive procedures should be kept to the minimum</p>
<p>73 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>viii. Artificial rupture of membranes should be avoided unless there is a good indication of the same.</p>
<p>ix. Observe the aseptic technique every time you are doing a sterile procedure</p>
<p>x. Avoid unnecessary frequent vaginal examinations.</p>
<p>I) Use partograph as appropriate for monitoring labour:</p>
<p>i. Observations about the condition of the pregnant woman, her unborn baby and progress of labor should be monitored regularly.</p>
<p>ii. Partograph should only be started when the mother is in active labor, ie cervical dilatation of 4cm has been achieved. The following observations are done: -</p>
<p>iii. Pulse rate: - recorded every 30 minutes when the woman is in active labor. Pulse rate of above 100b/m are indicative of anxiety, infections, ketosis or hemorrhage.</p>
<p>iv. Temperatures: - should be recorded every 4 hours. Pyrexia is indicative of infections or hypoglycemia.</p>
<p>v. Blood pressure: - measured every four hours, unless it is abnormal. Hypotension may be due to supine position, shock or epidural anaesthesia.</p>
<p>vi. Blood pressures may be further aggravated by labor on women who had hypertensive disorders in pregnancy.</p>
<p>vii. Urinalysis: - urine is tested for glucose, ketones and proteins. The volume of the urine is also measured.</p>
<p>viii. Contractions: - assessed Â½ hrly</p>
<p>ix. Descent of the presenting part: - assessed 4 hourly</p>
<p>x. Cervical dilatation: - assessed 4 hourly</p>
<p>xi. Fetal heart rate: - to assess fetal well being is assessed Â½ hourly</p>
<p>xii. Amniotic fluid: - It also determines the fetal reaction to labour and its assessed 4 hourly</p>
<p>m) Provide emotional support:</p>
<p>i. Listen to, encourage, support and reassure the woman continually</p>
<p>ii. Encourage the birth companion to support the woman emotionally during labor.</p>
<p>iii. Explain the process of labor to the woman and lay down expectations to relieve anxiety.</p>
<p>iv. Keep on encouraging the woman.</p>
<p>74 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>v. Express care and dependability to the client to boost her confidence.</p>
<p>vi. As a midwife, display tolerant non-judgmental attitude in provision of care</p>
<p>n) Promote nutrition during labour:</p>
<p>i. Offer the woman light foods rich in carbohydrates to provide energy during labor eg. Biscuits, toast, yoghurt, breakfast cereal, fruit juice, tea etc.</p>
<p>ii. Fluids intake will reduce the risk of dehydration during labor.</p>
<p>o) Control of pain may be achieved by non-pharmacological methods such as:</p>
<p>i. Change of position/ moving around,</p>
<p>ii. Touch and back massage from a companion</p>
<p>iii. Breathing techniques</p>
<p>iv. Verbal coaching and relaxation to help draw her attention away from labour pain</p>
<p>v. Warm bath or shower</p>
<p>p) Control of pain may be achieved by pharmacological methods such as:</p>
<p>i. Use of pharmacological agents e.g. tramadol 100mg 1M or slow IV 6-8 hourly, pethidine 50-100 mg 1M or IV slowly 6-8 hourly, inhalational nitrous oxide combined with 50% oxygen (Entonox) or epidural analgesia where available.</p>
<p>ii. Note that these drugs may depress foetal respiratory centres.</p>
<p>iii. NSAIDS (Such diclofenac, Ibuprofen) are not advised as they may suppress (inhibit) labour by interfering with prostaglandins production.</p>
<p>iv. Drugs that suppresses or inhibit labour are called tocolytics or Betamimetics.</p>
<p>q) Ensure privacy and confidentiality</p>
<p>r) Make arrangements to accommodate the birth companion or male partner</p>
<p>s) Anticipate the need for neonatal resuscitation and prepare for it</p>
<p>t) Prepare for management for the 2nd stages of labour</p>
<p>i. Environment-keep warm and close windows</p>
<p>ii. Equipment's-sterile pack and other accessories</p>
<p>iii. Staff-being prepared to conduct the delivery</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>iv. Suppliesâ€”should be adequate.</p>
<p>v. Resuscitative equipment in working conditionsâ€”sucker, oxygen, warmers/heaters</p>
<p>vi. Observe for signs of 2nd stage of labour: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Strong expulsive uterine contraction.</li>
<li>A trickle of blood</li>
<li>Full cervical dilation</li>
<li>Pouting and gaping of the anus</li>
<li>Gaping of the vulva in primigravida. The vulva of multiparous will gape even in premature pushing</li>
<li>Tenseness between the anus and coccyx</li>
<li>Bulging of the perineum usually means delivery is imminent</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-stage-of-labour">SECOND STAGE OF LABOUR.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Definition:</strong></p>
<p>It is the stage from full dilatation of the cervix (i.e. no cervix felt on V.E) until the Baby is born: -</p>
<p><strong>Duration:</strong></p>
<p>a) Primigravida 45 min â€“ 1 hour, as long as 2 hrs
b) Multigravida 1/2 hour can be as little as 5 minutes.</p>
<p>N.B. there should always be advance or descent in this stage</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-of-second-stage-of-labour">Signs of second stage of labour: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-of-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Presumptive signs</p>
<p>i. Dilatation and Gaping of the anus
ii. Rupture of the forewaters
iii. Show, appearance of the presenting part
iv. Strong expulsive uterine contraction.
v. A trickle of blood
vi. Pouting and gaping of the anus
vii. Gaping of the vulva in primigravida. The vulva of multiparous will gape even in premature pushing
viii. Tenseness between the anus and coccyx
ix. Bulging of the perineum usually means delivery is imminent
x. Visualization of fetal presenting part at the vulva</p>
<p>76 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>b) Confirmatory signs
i. No cervix felt on Vaginal examination</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiology-of-second-stage-of-labour">Physiology of second stage of labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiology-of-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Physiology of second stage of labour includes: -
a) Expulsive contractions
b) Urge to push
c) Secondary powers become active
d) Displacement of pelvic floor and soft tissue
e) Rectum compressed against sacrocurve
f) Fetal expulsion
g) Bulging of vulva and perineum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-second-stage-of-labour">Management of second stage of labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Once the patient is in the second stage the midwife must not LEAVE HER, and a constant and careful supervision must be kept on her:</p>
<ul>
<li>General condition, pulse, uterine contractions &amp; Vulva</li>
<li>Bladder should be empty</li>
<li>Fetal heart more frequently (after every contraction)</li>
<li>Descent of the presenting part and progress.</li>
<li>Membrane should be ruptured</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Transfer the mother to second stage room/couch
c) Ensure you have sterile delivery pack and other supplies
d) Support and explain to the mother expectations of second stage
e) Ask the assistant to open the sterile pack.
f) Gown and don gloves
g) Drape the mother procedurally
h) Perform vagina swab (procedurally)</p>
<p>77 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>i) Perform a V.E to confirm second stage
j) Encouraged her to bear down only during contractions and relax in between
k) Support perineum with a pad firmly at crowning (avoid obstructing the presenting part and allow foetal head to extend the perineum)
l) Ask the assistant to monitor FHR after every contraction
m) Encourage the mother to breath through the mouth after a contraction.
n) Avoid routine episiotomy</p>
<p>o) Delivery of the head:</p>
<p>Control birth of the foetal head by placing the fingers of one hand against the baby's head to keep it flexed.</p>
<p>Continue to support the perineum gently as the baby's head is born.</p>
<p>After the head is delivered, check for the cord around the neck. If present but loose, slip it over the baby's head.</p>
<p>If the cord is tight around the neck doubly clamp and cut it before unwinding it from the head.</p>
<p>Allow the baby's head to turn spontaneously (Restitution).</p>
<p>Once the head is delivered ask the patient not to push. Clear the airway of the newborn gently with sterile swab</p>
<p>p) Delivery of the body</p>
<p>Deliver one shoulder at a time.</p>
<p>With a hand on each side of the baby's head, move the head posteriorly to deliver the anterior shoulder and vice versa.</p>
<p>Place the baby on the mother's abdomen and congratulate the mother.</p>
<p>q) Perform APGAR scoring and show the baby to the mother.
r) Show the mother the baby and Let her confirm the sex of the baby.
s) Clamp and cut the cord (DO NOT MILK THE CORD)
t) Hand over the baby to the assistant and give instructions.</p>
<p>78 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>u) NB: If there is difficulty in delivering the shoulders suspect shoulder dystocia. DO NOT USE FORCE. Support the baby's body as it slides out and place the baby on the mother's abdomen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immediate-care-of-the-newborn">Immediate care of the newborn.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immediate-care-of-the-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Thoroughly but gently dry the baby
b) Keep the baby warm
c) Check breathing (Baby should be crying or breathing quietly and easily)
d) Vitamin K. 1mg (for a term baby)
e) Encourage breastfeeding and routine newborn care.
f) Anticipate the need for neonatal resuscitation and prepare in advance for it.
g) Apply an identification tag and wrap baby in warm soft, dry towels and give to the mother to initiate breastfeeding within the first one hour of life.
h) Once stable, perform 1st examination of the newborn.
i) To prevent ophthalmia neonatorum, apply 1% tetracycline eye ointment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="third-stage-of-labour">THIRD STAGE OF LABOUR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Definition.</p>
<p>Third stage of labour begins immediately after the baby is born, until the placenta is delivered. The third stage lasts between 5-15 minutes but any period up to 1 hour is normal. If it lasts more than 1 hr it is considered as retained placenta.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiology-of-third-stage-of-labour">Physiology of third stage of labour.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiology-of-third-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Physiology of third stage of labour include: -</p>
<ol>
<li>Separation of the placenta</li>
<li>Descent of the placenta</li>
<li>Expulsion of the placenta</li>
<li>Control of bleeding</li>
</ol>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="separation-of-the-placenta">Separation of the placenta<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#separation-of-the-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Separation of placenta is brought about by: -</p>
<p>a) Mechanical factors (It is brought by the contraction and retraction of the uterine muscles, the uterine contractions detach the placenta from the uterus and the placenta forced out of the upper uterine segment into the lower uterine segment.</p>
<p>In summary, the following mechanical factors come into play during the third stage of labour: -</p>
<ul>
<li>The uterus reduces in size 2.5cm below the umbilicus, or 15cm above the symphysis pubis after the expulsion of the foetus</li>
<li>The contraction and retraction of the uterine muscles continues</li>
<li>The placental site is reduced to half</li>
<li>Since the placenta is inelastic, it does not contract, so it detaches from the shrinking uterine wall</li>
<li>The placenta is pushed further to the lower uterine segment by the weight of the retro-placental clot. This is the accumulated blood from the separated placenta</li>
<li>With the next contraction the placenta is pushed into the vagina and expelled</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Haemostatic factors. At the area of the separation the blood sinuses are torn across. 30 to 60ml of blood is connected between maternal surface of the placenta and the decidual basalis. This blood clots further assisting in separation of placenta.</p>
<p>There are two main methods of placental separation:</p>
<p>a) Central (Schultze) separation
b) Marginal (Mathews Duncan) separation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schultze-central-separation">Schultze (Central) Separation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schultze-central-separation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Separation begins at the center of the placenta and at the area of separation there is formation of retro-placental clots that aids in separation of the placenta by exerting pressure at the midpoint of placental attachment.</p>
<p>It is associated with minimal blood loss.</p>
<p>Placenta is expelled with foetal side exposed.</p>
<p>80 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-911d5d13.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marginal-mathews-duncan-separation">Marginal (Mathews Duncan) separation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marginal-mathews-duncan-separation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Separation starts at the lower edge of placenta (asymmetrical/lateral border separates)</p>
<p>There is bleeding associated with this method because there is no formation of retro-placental clots.</p>
<p>Placenta is expelled with maternal side exposed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="duncan-mechanism">Duncan mechanism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#duncan-mechanism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-e2ec4a10.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schultze-mechanism">Schultze mechanism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schultze-mechanism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-6a73bc44.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<p>81 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-of-placental-separation">Signs of placental separation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-of-placental-separation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Signs of placental separation are: -</p>
<p>a) Elongation of the cord
b) The cord doesn't recede with pressure on the symphysis pubis
c) A gush of blood
d) Visualization of the placenta on birth canal
e) Uterus contracts and becomes globular (like a cricket ball)
f) Fundus rises at the level of umbilicus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="descent-of-the-placenta">Descent of the placenta<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#descent-of-the-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When the placenta has completely separated the following mechanisms pushes the placenta down(descent) into the lower uterine segment and into the vagina: -</p>
<p>a) Uterine contraction and retraction (contracting uterus pushes it down into the lower uterine segment and into the vagina)
b) Weight of the placenta.</p>
<p>Signs of placental descent may include: -</p>
<p>a) The uterus becomes hard and movable
b) The fundus rises to the level of the umbilicus
c) Cord does not recede with suprapubic pressure
d) Placenta can be felt On vaginal examination or can be visualized at the vulva.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="expulsion-of-the-placenta">Expulsion of the placenta.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expulsion-of-the-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the expulsion of the placenta from the uterus.</p>
<p>It can occur through the following ways: -</p>
<p>a) Controlled cord traction</p>
<p>An oxytocic drug is given (10 I.U IM), if pregnancy is not multiple as soon as anterior shoulder is delivered.</p>
<p>The cord is clamped and cut, wait for contraction.</p>
<p>PageNORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>Do not wait for the sign of placental separation and descent</p>
<p>As soon as the uterus contracts the left hand is placed above the symphysis pubis push and the uterus upwards towards the umbilicus. At the same time the right hand grasps the umbilical cord and apply traction in â€œa down ward directionâ€ and then deliver the placenta.</p>
<p>b) Maternal effort
c) Fundal pressure
d) Gravity and intra-abdominal pressure (Traditional method)</p>
<p>NB-Each student to read more on the other three methods of placental expulsion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="control-of-bleeding">Control of bleeding.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-of-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Processes that control bleeding during third stage of labour include: -</p>
<p>a) Contraction &amp; relaxation of uterine muscles
b) The actions of living ligatures
c) Extra clotting power in the blood.
d) Activation of coagulation mechanisms and Fibrinolysis system.</p>
<p>Contraction and retraction of uterine muscles causes the placental site to reduce into half and this causes Criss-cross fibres to control bleeding by compressing the blood vessels. There is also retraction of the oblique muscle fibres in upper segment which further helps in stopping bleeding. Living ligatures" The oblique muscles fibers of the uterus run in and out between the blood vessels when the uterus is contracted they clump the blood vessels very securely and the bleeding stops.</p>
<p>Clotting of blood takes place in the sinuses sealing the bleeding points a few hours later when uterine contractions are less vigorous. This will lead to activation of: Coagulation pathway and Fibrinolysis system. This leads to Achievement of hemostasis. The mother has extra clothing power in her blood at this time the clotting mechanism is very powerful.</p>
<p>The midwife should be aware that the third stage is the shortest and easiest but the most dangerous stage.</p>
<p>At the end of the third stage:</p>
<p>a) The uterus should be hard, round and movable
b) The uterus should be mid-way between the umbilicus and symphysis pubis</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>c) There should be no excessive bleeding
d) The bladder should be empty</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clamping-and-cutting-of-the-umbilical-cord">Clamping and cutting of the umbilical cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clamping-and-cutting-of-the-umbilical-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two approaches in clamping and cutting the umbilical cord during delivery, namely:</p>
<p>a) Early/immediate cord clamping
b) Delayed cord clamping.</p>
<p>NB: Each student to read more on each approach</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="active-management-of-the-third-stage-of-labour-amtsl">Active Management of the Third Stage of Labour (AMTSL)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#active-management-of-the-third-stage-of-labour-amtsl" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Palpate the abdomen to rule out the presence of an additional baby before initiating AMSTL</p>
<p>AMTSL includes:</p>
<p>a) Prophylactic use of oxytocin (Uterotonins or Oxytocic drugs)
b) Controlled cord traction for delivery of the placenta
c) Uterine massage</p>
<p>Use of Uterotonins or Oxytocic drugs during third stage of labour helps in:</p>
<p>a) Speeding up the delivery of the placenta
b) Lessening the blood loss
c) Contracting the uterus</p>
<p>Oxytocin is preferred because: -</p>
<p>a) It is potent and easy to titrate
b) It has a short half-life (one to five minutes)
c) It is generally well tolerated</p>
<p>Examination of the placenta.</p>
<p>It is important for the midwife to examine placenta. Examination of placenta helps in determining:</p>
<ol>
<li>Completeness of the placenta</li>
<li>Possibility of a missing or extra lobe</li>
<li>To detect any placental abnormalities</li>
</ol>
<p>During examination of the placenta, the midwife should be able inspect: -</p>
<p>a) Maternal surface and fetal surfaces
b) Cord â€“ B/vessels, insertion, length, knots,
c) Membrane-chorion and amnion</p>
<p>84 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>d) Weigh
e) Blood loss estimation</p>
<p>f) Placental abnormalities such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Structural â€“ succenturiate lobe, circumvallate, bipartite and tripartite, battledore and velamentous insertion of cord.</li>
<li>Disease related abnormalities â€“ infarcts, syphilitic, oedematous, calcification, tumours.</li>
<li>Placental implantation: Placenta praevia, placenta accreta, increta, percreta, vasa praevia.</li>
</ul>
<p>The midwife should ensure proper documentation and feedback of the findings.</p>
<p>The midwife should remember the following properties of a placenta:
a) Circular in shape, approx. 20 cm diameter, and 2.5 cm thick.
b) It weighs about 500g and is dark red in colour.
c) Develops from 14th day -16th wk
d) Its divided into 15 to 20 lobes by deep grooves.
e) The umbilical cord has two arteries and one vein</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fourth-stage-of-labour">FOURTH STAGE OF LABOUR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fourth-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Immediate Care of Mother:
a) The mother and the baby has to remain in the delivery room for an hour after delivery.
b) Give oxytocin 5-10 iu, massage the uterus and expel the clots.
c) The vulva is swabbed and a sterile pad placed in position
d) Buttocks should be dry and any wet sheet is removed the sterile towel is removed over the lower abdomen and thighs and cover with warm blanket.
e) Careful observation: Check the maternal pulse (60-70) minute is the normal range, take body temperature â€“ subnormal due to loss of body heat, as high as 37.2Â°C due to reactions of prolonged labour, Blood pressure is taken Â½ hourly
f) Encourage her to pass urine / Frequent emptying of the bladder.
g) Give her a hot drink and place the baby on the breast
h) Perform Physical examination</p>
<p>85 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>i) Examination of birth canal for tears
j) Carefully examine the cervix, vagina and perineum and repair any tears present as appropriate. Repair the episiotomy and tears. Explain all procedures to the mother.
k) Observe the mother every 15 minutes for vital signs and vaginal bleeding.
l) Perform Mental status assessment
m) Assess lochia and blood loss
n) Breast examination for establishment of lactation
o) Pain management
p) Treat or refer if any complications are detected.
q) Check for calf tenderness
r) Educate the mother to report any bleeding</p>
<p>Immediate care of baby:
a) Keep the baby warm
b) Thoroughly but gently dry the baby
c) Check breathing (Baby should be crying or breathing quietly and easily)
d) Observe her general wellbeing of the baby
e) Monitor the newborn's condition for bleeding from the cord, maintenance of body temperature and where appropriate, encourage initiation of breastfeeding
f) Check the security of the cord clamp
g) Check APGAR score
h) Promote bonding and breast feeding
i) Put on ID (identification) band
j) Check weight, height, head circumference and any drug(s) given to the baby
k) Vitamin K. 1mg (for a term baby)
l) Apply an identification tag and wrap baby in warm soft, dry towels and give to the mother to initiate breastfeeding within the first one hour of life.
m) Once stable, perform 1st examination of the newborn.</p>
<p>86 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>n) To prevent ophthalmia neonatorum, apply 1% tetracycline eye ointment.</p>
<p>Educate the mother on:-</p>
<p>a) Postnatal HIV counseling and testing.
b) Exclusive breastfeeding
c) Family planning
d) Post natal danger signs
e) Personal hygiene
f) Proper nutrition
g) Exercises
h) Care of the perineum
i) Use of LLITNs
j) Immunization
k) Bonding
l) Kangaroo care (In case of a preterm baby).
m) Return date and FANC visits</p>
<p>Proper documentation and Record keeping: -</p>
<p>Record your observations during labour to include:</p>
<p>a) Method of delivery- spontaneous or accelerated, forceps, cesarean section or vacuum.
b) Anaesthetic - General, epidural, local
c) Blood loss- amount
d) Placenta and membranes- complete, incomplete
e) Perineum- laceration, episiotomy
f) Drugs given for the mother
g) Baby - Sex, weight, APGAR score, alive or stillbirth. Date and time of delivery</p>
<p>N. B. The chart should present a clear, concise, reliable record.</p>
<p>h) The legal aspect of record keeping is also important during labour.</p>
<p>Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="partograph">PARTOGRAPH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#partograph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition.</p>
<p>It is the graphical analysis of labour for clinical evaluation of the progress of labour. It's a graphic presentation, which outlines the progress of a woman in active labour including the foetal and maternal condition.</p>
<p>It serves as a management tool used for the detection of abnormal progress of labour. Used for assessment of:</p>
<p>a) Fetal well being
b) Maternal well being
c) Progress of labor</p>
<p>It has two important lines:</p>
<p>a) Alert line
b) Action line</p>
<p>Pertograph begins to be plotted at four centimeter dilatation.</p>
<p>Alert line begins at 4cm and extends to full dilatation.</p>
<p>Action line is an important line as it guides a midwife on when labour is progressing poorly and an intervention is required.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-using-partograph">Advantages of using partograph.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-using-partograph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>It helps in estimating expected time of delivery</li>
<li>It can detect any impending problem/danger during labour</li>
<li>It helps in detecting delayed labour</li>
<li>It ensures continued care and monitoring of mothers in labour</li>
<li>Can be used in giving report during change of shift</li>
<li>It simplifies transfer of clients to higher health facilities</li>
<li>It is useful in statistical analysis of labour</li>
<li>It can be used as training tool.</li>
</ol>
<p>88 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="information-recorded-on-the-partograph">Information recorded on the partograph<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#information-recorded-on-the-partograph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Information recorded on the partograph includes:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Patient information:
a) Full Name, age, gravidity, parity, hospital number, date and time of admission and time of rupture of the membranes in hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foetal Condition:
a) The Foetal heart rate observed Â½ hourly and plotted with a dot (.).
b) The normal foetal heart rate is between 120 - 160 beats per minute.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amniotic fluid and membranes</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Record the state of the membranes and/or amniotic fluid /liquor on the partograph in the area provided as follows:
a) I - Intact membranes
b) C - Clear liquor on ruptured membranes
c) M - Meconium stained liquor
d) A - Absent liquor if membranes are ruptured
e) B - Blood stained liquor.</p>
<p>This observation is made at each vaginal examination. If there is thick meconium at any time or absent liquor at the time of membrane rupture, rule out other signs of foetal distress and take appropriate action.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Moulding of the foetal skull bones</li>
</ol>
<p>An indication of how adequately the pelvis can accommodate the foetal head. Increasing moulding with the head high in the pelvis is a sign of cephalopelvic disproportion.</p>
<p>Moulding is observed 4 hourly in the row indicated moulding:
a) 0 If bones are separated and the sutures can be felt easily
b) + If sutures are apposed but no overlap i.e. the bones are just touching each other
c) ++ If there is overlapping of the sutures but it is reducible
d) +++ If the sutures overlap but not reducible</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Cervical dilation</li>
</ol>
<p>89 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<p>a) Assessed at every vaginal examination and is plotted with an (X).
b) The first vaginal examination, on admission, includes a pelvic assessment. Thereafter, vaginal examinations are done every 4 hours, unless contraindicated or as indicated e.g. if 2nd stage is imminent or there is evidence of rapid progress of labour as may occur in multiparous patients.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Descent of the foetal head</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Measured by abdominal palpation and is expressed in terms of fifths palpable above the pelvic brim.
b) Its plotted with an (O)</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Hours:</li>
</ol>
<p>a) This refers to the time elapsed since onset of active phase of labour (observed or extrapolated)</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Time:
a) This refers to actual time</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uterine Contractions</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>In normal labour the uterine contractions increase in frequency and intensity. The number of the uterine contractions is assessed and recorded every half-hour in the active phase of labour.</p>
<p>b) The frequency: How often are they felt (i.e. the number of contractions palpated in ten minutes.)
c) The duration: How long do they last (in seconds); the duration must also be palpated not just estimated by observation. Duration are expressed as follows:</p>
<p>i. Less than 20 seconds: Mild
ii. Between 20 and 40 seconds: Moderate
iii. More than 40 seconds: Strong</p>
<p>Shading of uterine contraction duration on a partograph.</p>
<p>Contractions on a partograph are shaded as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Mild contractions</li>
<li>Moderate contractions</li>
<li>Strong contractions</li>
</ol>
<p>90 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<ol start="10">
<li>Maternal Condition</li>
</ol>
<p>Entered at the foot of the partograph, below the recording of the uterine contractions and include:</p>
<p>a) Oxytocin regime: Indicates the amount of oxytocin per volume intravenous fluid as well as the rate of administration in drops per minute.</p>
<p>b) Drugs and IV fluids: Record here any additional drugs administered during labour</p>
<p>c) Pulse rate: Maternal pulse rate is observed every half hourly and marked with a dot (-)</p>
<p>d) Blood Pressure: This is taken once every 4 hours and indicated with arrows for diastolic and systolic reading joined with a dotted line</p>
<p>e) Temperature: Ideally the temperature in C should be taken every 2 hours and recorded in the space provided</p>
<p>f) Urine: Encourage the woman to pass urine every 2-4 hours. Measure the volume of urine passed and check it for protein and acetone. Record in the space provided at the bottom of the partograph</p>
<p>91 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sample-of-a-partograph">Sample of a Partograph.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sample-of-a-partograph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260128-efc40c62.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg">
92 | Page NORMAL MIDWIFERY LECTURE NOTES - RUGENDO</p>
